Resolving Conflicts: Explicit Correction and the Primacy of Imam Abu Hanifa
Refines the hierarchy with conditions on explicit vs implicit taṣḥīḥ and the priority of the Imam's statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit (ṣarīḥ) and implicit (iltizāmī) taṣḥīḥ and state when the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa takes precedence over other views.

Core Idea
Explicit correction overrides a matn's implicit endorsement; but the Imam's own statement always prevails when verifications cancel out.

The basic hierarchy provides a clear order, but what happens when a matn contains a ruling without explicitly saying it is the correct view, while a later scholar explicitly corrects it? This lesson delves into the crucial distinction between explicit and implicit taṣḥīḥ (verification). Additionally, when two verifications conflict and neutralize each other, the fallback is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa himself, as the master of the school. These nuances ensure precision in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two types of taṣḥīḥ
Taṣḥīḥ can be ṣarīḥ (explicit) when a scholar says 'al-ṣaḥīḥ kadha', or iltizāmī (implicit) when a matn simply includes a ruling as the school's position without commentary.
The matn's inclusion is an implicit undertaking that it is the correct view.
2
Learn the sub-rule: explicit over implicit
According to al-ʿAllāmah Qāsim, if the matn implicitly adopts a view and a later source explicitly corrects the opposite, the explicit correction takes precedence.
This is because explicit verification is stronger.
3
Recognize the primacy of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement
When two verifications conflict and cancel each other out, one returns to the original principle: the Imam's statement is preferred over that of his disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) or later scholars.
The passage quotes that giving fatwa by the Imam's statement is obligatory unless necessity dictates otherwise.
4
Identify the exception for necessity
In rare cases like muzara'ah (sharecropping), the school may adopt the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to necessity, even though the general rule prefers the Imam.
This exception is well-known in the school.
5
Apply the combined rule to a scenario
Given a matn with an implicit ruling, a fatwa explicitly correcting it, and also a conflicting statement from Imam Abu Hanifa versus his students, determine which view prevails.
Follow the hierarchy: explicit correction > matn's implicit; within same level, Imam's statement > others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة الثالثة: طبقات المسائل ومحمد بن سلمة ونصير بن يحيى، وذكر فيها اختياراته أيضاً، وهو أصل الواقعات. ثم جمع المشايخ فيه كتباً: كـ«مجموع النوازل والواقعات» للنَّاطِفِي والصدر الشهيد وغيره. ثمَّ جمع من بعدهم من المشايخ هذه الطبقات في فتاواهم مختلطة غير ممتازة، كما في «جامع قاضي خان»، و«الخلاصة»، وغيرهما من كتب الفتاوى، وقد ميّز بعضُهم كما في «المحيط» لرضي الدين السِّرَخْسِي فإنه بدأ بمسائل الأصول أولاً، ثم النوادر ثم الفتاوى. انتهى كلامه. وقد ذكرتُ بعض ما يتعلّق بهذا البحث في «مقدمة الهداية»، وفي «النافع الكبير لمن يطالع الجامع الصغير»، فليرجع إليهما.
واعلم أنهم ذكروا عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية أي إن كبار علماء المذهب نصوا على ذلك، ومن أقوالهم ما يلي: قال الشرنبلالي في حاشيته على الدرر: ونحفظ عن مشايخنا تقديم ما في المتون والشروح على ما في الفتاوى. وقال الحموي في «غمز العيون»: العمل على ما في المتون إذا عارضه ما في الفتاوى. وقال الطرطوسي في «أنفع الوسائل»: إذا تعارض تصحيح ما في المتون والفتاوى فالمعتمد ما في المتون. انتهى. ينظر: غمز العيون (٤: ١٥٥). وقال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار: إذا اختلف التصحيح لقولين وكان أحدهما قول الإمام أو في المتون أخذ بما هو قول الإمام؛ لأنه صاحب المذهب، وبما في المتون؛ لأنها موضوعة لنقل المذهب. وقال فيه: متى اختلف الترجيح رجح ما في المتون. وقال فيه أيضاً: والمتون مقدمة على الشروح. وقال فيه أيضاً: في قضاء الفوائت من البحر أنه إذا اختلف التصحيح والفتوى فالعمل بما وافق المتون أولى. انتهى. وكذا لو كان أحدهما في الشروح والآخر في الفتاوى لما صرحوا به من أن ما في المتون مقدم على ما في الشروح وما في الشروح مقدم على ما في الفتاوى، لكن هذا عند التصريح بتصحيح كل من القولين أو عدم التصريح أصلاً. أما لو ذكرت مسألة المتون لم يصرحوا بتصحيحها بل صرحوا بتصحيح مقابلها، فقد أفاد العلامة قاسم ترجيح الثاني؛ لأنه تصحيح صريح وما في المتون تصحيح التزامي، والتصحيح الصريح مقدم على التصحيح الالتزامي: أي التزام المتون ذكر ما هو الصحيح في المذهب. وكذا لا تخيير لو كان أحدهما قول الإمام والآخر قول غيره؛ لأنه لما تعارض التصحيحان تساقطا، فرجعنا إلى الأصل وهو تقديم قول الإمام. بل في شهادات الفتاوى الخيرية: المقرر عندنا أنه لا يفتى ويعمل إلا بقول الإمام الأعظم، ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما أو قول أحدهما أو غيرهما إلا لضرورة كمسألة المزارعة، وإن صرح المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قولهما؛ لأنه صاحب المذهب والإمام المقدم. انتهى. ومثله في البحر عند الكلام على أوقات الصلاة. وفيه من كتاب القضاء: يحل الإفتاء بقول الإمام، بل يجب وإن لم يعلم من أين قال. انتهى. وقال ابن نجيم في البحر الرائق: العمل على ما هو في المتون؛ لأنه إذا تعارض ما في المتون والفتاوى فالمعتمد ما في المتون، وكذا يقدم ما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى. وقال فيه: والإفتاء بما في المتون أولى. وقال الحصكفي في الدر المنتقى: والإفتاء بما في المتون أولى. وقال في الدر المختار: ورجح في الشرنبلالية بأن ما في المتون والشروح أولى بما في كتب الفتاوى فليحفظ. وقال التمرتاشي في منح الغفار: إن اختلف التصحيح، فالمعتمد ما في المتون.
The third study: Layers of legal issues, and Muhammad ibn Salamah and Nasir ibn Yahya, and he mentioned therein his selections also, and it is the origin of incidents. Then the scholars compiled books on it: such as 'Majmu' al-Nawazil wa al-Waqi'at' by al-Natifi and al-Sadr al-Shahid and others. Then the later scholars compiled these layers in their fatwas mixed without distinction, as in 'Jami' Qadi Khan' and 'al-Khulasah' and other books of fatwas, and some distinguished as in 'al-Muhit' by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, for he began with issues of the principles first, then the rare reports, then the fatwas. His speech ends. And I have mentioned some of what pertains to this research in 'Muqaddimat al-Hidayah' and in 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir li man Yutali' al-Jami' al-Saghir', so refer to them. And know that they mentioned in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah' that the senior scholars of the school stated that, and from their statements are the following: Al-Shurnbalali said in his gloss on al-Durar: We have preserved from our teachers the precedence of what is in the matns and commentaries over what is in the fatwas. And al-Hamawi said in 'Ghamz al-'Uyun': The practice is upon what is in the matns when what is in the fatwas contradicts it. And al-Tartusi said in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il': If there is a conflict in verification between what is in the matns and the fatwas, the relied-upon is what is in the matns. End. See: Ghamz al-'Uyun (4:155). And Ibn 'Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar: If verification differs on two statements and one of them is the Imam's statement or is in the matns, one takes what is the Imam's statement, because he is the master of the school, and what is in the matns, because they are established to transmit the school. And he said in it: Whenever the preference differs, prefer what is in the matns. And he also said in it: The matns are given precedence over the commentaries. And he also said in it: In 'Qada' al-Fawa'it' from al-Bahr, that if verification and fatwa differ, then practice in accordance with what agrees with the matns is better. End. And likewise if one is in the commentaries and the other in the fatwas, because they stated that what is in the matns is given precedence over what is in the commentaries, and what is in the commentaries is given precedence over what is in the fatwas. But this is when explicit verification of each of the two statements is given, or no verification at all. As for if the matn mentions an issue without explicit verification, but they explicitly verify its opposite, then al-'Allamah Qasim stated the preference of the second, because it is explicit verification and what is in the matn is implicit verification, and explicit verification takes precedence over implicit verification: i.e., the matn's implicit undertaking to mention what is correct in the school. And likewise there is no option if one is the Imam's statement and the other is another's statement, because when verifications conflict they cancel out, so we return to the principle which is giving precedence to the Imam's statement. Rather, in 'Shahadat' of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah: The established view with us is that no fatwa is given nor practice carried out except by the statement of the Great Imam, and one does not deviate from it to their statement or the statement of one of them or others except for necessity, like the issue of muzara'ah, even if the scholars explicitly state that the fatwa is upon their statement, because he is the master of the school and the leading Imam. End. And similarly in al-Bahr when discussing the times of prayer. And in it from the Book of Judgments: It is permissible to give fatwa by the Imam's statement, rather it is obligatory even if one does not know from where he said it. End. And Ibn Nujaym said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Practice is upon what is in the matns, because if what is in the matns and the fatwas conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the matns, and likewise what is in the commentaries is given precedence over what is in the fatwas. And he said in it: And giving fatwa by what is in the matns is better. And al-Haskafi said in al-Durr al-Muntaqa: And giving fatwa by what is in the matns is better. And he said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: And it was preferred in al-Shurnabulaliyyah that what is in the matns and commentaries is better than what is in the fatwa books, so let it be memorized. And al-Timurtashi said in Minah al-Ghaffar: If verification differs, the relied-upon is what is in the matns.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage covers a foundational methodological principle in the Hanafi school: the hierarchy of textual sources. The author first introduces the concept of 'layers' (tabaqāt) of legal issues, explaining how early scholars like Muhammad ibn Salamah and Nasir ibn Yahya compiled the foundational texts (uṣūl) and rare reports (nawādir), and how later scholars mixed these layers in their fatwa collections. He then presents the critical rule: when there is a conflict, priority is given first to the matn (core text), then to the sharḥ (commentary), and finally to fatwa collections. He supports this with numerous quotes from leading Hanafi jurists: al-Shurnbulālī, al-Ḥamawī, al-Ṭarṭūsī, Ibn ʿĀbidīn, Ibn Nujaym, al-Ḥaṣkafī, al-Tīmurtāshī, and others. An important nuance is added by al-ʿAllāmah Qāsim: if a matn mentions a ruling implicitly without explicit correction, but a fatwa explicitly corrects the opposite, the explicit correction takes precedence because it is explicit versus implicit. Furthermore, if one statement is from Imam Abū Ḥanīfa and another from a different imam, the Imam's word prevails, as he is the master of the school. This hierarchy is not absolute; necessity may require deviating from the Imam's view, as in the case of muzāraʿah (sharecropping). The passage also notes that giving fatwa by the Imam's statement is not only permissible but sometimes obligatory, even without knowing the exact evidence. This rule ensures consistency and authority in the school's legal practice.

Key Terms
تصحيح (taṣḥīḥ): The process of establishing which among conflicting opinions is the correct (ṣaḥīḥ) view for the school. It can be explicit (ṣarīḥ) or implicit (iltizāmī) when the matn adopts a particular view.
قول الإمام (qawl al-Imām): The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, the founder of the school, which is given primacy over the statements of his disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) unless necessity dictates otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when taṣḥīḥ statements conflict and cancel each other out, what is the default principle?
A) Prefer the view of Abu Yusuf.
B) Prefer the view of Imam Abu Hanifa.
C) Prefer the view of the later scholar.
D) The mufti may choose any view.

Key Takeaway
When a matn implicitly adopts a view, an explicit correction from a later authority overrides it; and when verifications conflict, the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is the default.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Source Hierarchy (Matn, Sharh, Fatawa)
Establishes the hierarchy of Hanafi legal sources with authoritative quotations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of Hanafi textual sources and explain the precedence of matn over sharh and fatawa.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, matn rules unless a lower source explicitly corrects it.

This lesson presents the foundational hierarchy of Hanafi legal texts as established by the school's major scholars. When a ruling in a matn conflicts with a ruling in a sharh or fatawa, the matn takes precedence. This principle is supported by numerous authorities including al-Shurunbulali, al-Hamawi, Ibn Abidin, and others. The hierarchy ensures consistency and preserves the school's core teachings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three tiers
The Hanafi school categorizes its literature into three main tiers: mutun (core texts like al-Hidayah and al-Quduri), shuruh (commentaries), and fatawa (later fatwa collections). Each tier has a different level of authority.
Some also include a fourth tier for qanun but this lesson focuses on these three.
2
Understand the default hierarchy
When rulings conflict, the default order is: matn > sharh > fatawa. This means a ruling found in a matn takes precedence over a contrary ruling in a sharh, and a sharh ruling takes precedence over a fatwa.
This is the general rule, but there are exceptions.
3
Recognize the authority of the Imam's statement
If one of the conflicting rulings is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa (the founder of the madhhab), it takes precedence over the statements of his students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), unless necessity dictates otherwise.
This is because the Imam is the primary authority of the madhhab.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a conflict
Given a hypothetical conflict — for example, al-Hidayah (matn) states that a sale is valid without specifying the price, but a later fatwa says it is invalid — the mufti should follow al-Hidayah unless the fatwa explicitly corrects it.

And know that they mentioned: Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya (1) meaning that the senior scholars of the madhhab stated that, and from their statements are the following: Al-Shurunbulali said in his marginalia on al-Durar (2): 276: 'We preserve from our teachers the precedence of what is in the matn and sharh over what is in the fatawa.' Al-Hamawi said in Ghumz al-'Uyun (1): 334: 'The operative ruling is what is in the matn if it conflicts with what is in the fatawa.' Al-Tartusi said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: 'If correction in the matn and fatawa conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the matn.' End. See Ghumz al-'Uyun (4:155).
Ibn Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar (4): 33: 'If correction differs for two statements and one of them is the statement of the Imam or in the matn, the statement of the Imam is taken because he is the founder of the madhhab, and what is in the matn because they are established for transmitting the madhhab.' And he said in it (1:489): 'Whenever tarjih differs, what is in the matn is given preponderance.' And he said in it (2): 299 also: 'Matn are given precedence over sharh.' And he said in it (1): 77 also: 'In (Qada' al-Fawa'it) from al-Bahr, that if correction and fatwa conflict, acting upon what agrees with the matn is more appropriate.' End. And likewise if one of them is in the sharh and the other in the fatawa, because they stated that what is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa. But this is when there is explicit correction of each of the two statements or no correction at all. As for if the matter of the matn is mentioned without explicit correction but the opposite is explicitly corrected, then al-Allama Qasim indicated giving preponderance to the second because it is explicit correction, and what is in the matn is implicit correction, and explicit correction takes precedence over implicit correction: meaning the matn's obligation to mention what is correct in the madhhab. And likewise there is no choice if one is the statement of the Imam and the other is the statement of someone else, because when the two corrections conflict they cancel each other out, so we revert to the principle of giving precedence to the statement of the Imam. Rather, in 'Shahadat' of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya: 'It is established with us that no fatwa or action is taken except according to the statement of the Great Imam, and it is not deviated from to their statement or the statement of one of them or others except for necessity like the case of muzara'ah, even if the scholars state that the fatwa is on their statement, because he is the founder of the madhhab and the most advanced Imam.' End. And similar is in al-Bahr when discussing the times of prayer, and in it from the Book of Qada': 'It is permissible to give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam, rather it is obligatory even if one does not know from where he said.' End. Ibn Nujaym said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (6): 310: 'The operative ruling is what is in the matn, because if what is in the matn and the fatawa conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the matn. And likewise what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa.' And he said in it (3): 142: 'Giving fatwa according to what is in the matn is more appropriate.' Al-Haskafi said in al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1): 341: 'Giving fatwa according to what is in the matn is more appropriate.' And he said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar (5): 452: 'It is given preponderance in al-Shurunbulaliyya that what is in the matn and sharh is more appropriate than what is in the books of fatawa, so let it be memorized.'
Al-Timirtashi said in Manh al-Ghaffar (3107/2/b): 'If correction differs, the relied-upon is what is in the matn.'

The third study: Layers of Mas'ails
45
Indeed, what is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh over what is in the fatawa. So if a mas'ala is found in the matn established for transmitting the madhhab and its opposite is found in the sharh, what is in the matn is taken. And if a conflict occurs between what is in the sharh and what is in the fatwa, what is in the sharh is taken. But this is when there is no explicit correction in the lower layer.
(1)
Shaykh Amin, author of Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar, said in Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya in the Book of Ijarah: 'Ibn Wahban (3) and others mentioned that no regard is given to what is said in al-Quniyya if it contradicts others, and they also said that what is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh over what is in the fatawa.' End.

Al-Lakhnawi also said in al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyya (p. 180): 'What is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh over what is in the fatawa... (1) meaning if it is explicitly stated in the sharh or fatawa that this statement is sahih, or asahh, or upon it is the fatwa, or by it fatwa is given, or by it we take, or other explicit phrases indicating the preponderance of this statement as stipulated in the books on the code of the mufti. Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This is a methodological discussion from the Hanafi fiqh tradition concerning the hierarchy of textual sources when conflicts arise in legal rulings. The passage establishes a clear principle: texts found in the core matn (such as al-Hidayah, al-Quduri) take precedence over those in sharh (commentaries), and sharh take precedence over fatawa (fatwa collections). This hierarchy is supported by quotations from major Hanafi authorities including al-Shurunbulali, al-Hamawi, al-Tartusi, Ibn Abidin, Ibn Nujaym, al-Haskafi, and al-Timirtashi.

The key nuance is that this precedence applies only when there is no explicit tashih (declaration of correctness) in the lower tier. If a sharh or fatwa collection explicitly states that a particular ruling is sahih, asahh, or that the fatwa is upon it, that explicit correction overrides the implicit correctness of the matn. This is because the matn's correctness is deemed 'iltizami' (implicit, by virtue of the matn's purpose to transmit the correct madhhab position), while a direct tashih is 'sarihi' (explicit). Explicit correction takes priority.

Additionally, if both corrections conflict, or if one is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa and the other of his students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the Imam's saying is given precedence because he is the founder of the madhhab. However, later scholars note that this rule is relaxed in cases of necessity, such as the issue of muzara'ah (sharecropping), where the fatwa is on the saying of the two students.

Ibn Abidin and others emphasize that this hierarchy is foundational. The passage concludes by citing al-Lakhnawi, who lists explicit phrases that constitute tashih sarih (explicit correction): 'this is sahih', 'asahh', 'upon it is the fatwa', 'by it fatwa is given', 'by it we take', etc.

In practice, this means a mufti or student should first consult the matn. If the ruling is not found there, or if there is a conflict, they should then consult the sharh, and finally fatawa collections. But if a lower-tier source explicitly corrects a ruling, that takes precedence over the matn's default position.

Key Terms
متون (mutun): Core authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab, such as al-Hidayah and al-Quduri, established for transmitting the school's positions.
شروح (shurūḥ): Commentaries on the mutun that explain, expand, or sometimes qualify the rulings found in the core texts.
فتاوى (fatāwā): Later fatwa collections that compile legal opinions of later Hanafi scholars, considered the lowest tier of textual authority.
تصحيح (taṣḥīḥ): The act of declaring a particular ruling as correct (sahih) within the madhhab. It can be explicit (sarihi) or implicit (iltizami).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct order of precedence in Hanafi sources when there is no explicit correction?
A) Fatawa > Sharh > Matn
B) Matn > Sharh > Fatawa
C) Sharh > Matn > Fatawa
D) No fixed hierarchy

Key Takeaway
Matn are the primary source, followed by shuruh, then fatawa, but explicit correction in a lower source can override the matn.

Method of Learning
intermediate

Exceptions: Explicit Tashih and the Imam's Statement
Explores exceptions to the source hierarchy, focusing on explicit tashih and the Imam's precedence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit and implicit tashih and explain when a lower-tier source can override a matn, and when the Imam's statement takes precedence.

Core Idea
Explicit correction trumps implicit; the Imam's word trumps all.

While the default hierarchy places matn above all, the Hanafi school recognizes two key exceptions: explicit tashih (correction) in a sharh or fatwa can override the matn, and the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa prevails over that of his students. This lesson explores these nuances with examples from the text, emphasizing the practical implications for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Understand tashih types
Tashih is the declaration that a particular ruling is correct. It can be explicit (sarihi) using phrases like 'sahih' or 'asahh', or implicit (iltizami) as the matn's inherent correctness.
Explicit tashih is stronger.
2
Know when explicit tashih overrides
If a sharh or fatwa explicitly corrects a ruling using one of the recognized phrases, it takes precedence over the matn. If not, the matn prevails.
The passage quotes al-Lakhnawi listing such phrases.
3
Recognize the authority of the Imam
The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa takes precedence over those of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, except in cases of necessity (e.g., muzara'ah). When corrections conflict and one is from the Imam, his view is chosen.
This is because he is the founder of the madhhab.
4
Apply the exception to a scenario
Given a matn ruling and an explicit correction in a sharh, decide to follow the sharh. Given a conflict between Imam's statement and students' statement, follow the Imam unless necessity dictates.

And know that they mentioned: Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya (1) meaning that the senior scholars of the madhhab stated that, and from their statements are the following: Al-Shurunbulali said in his marginalia on al-Durar (2): 276: 'We preserve from our teachers the precedence of what is in the matn and sharh over what is in the fatawa.' Al-Hamawi said in Ghumz al-'Uyun (1): 334: 'The operative ruling is what is in the matn if it conflicts with what is in the fatawa.' Al-Tartusi said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: 'If correction in the matn and fatawa conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the matn.' End. See Ghumz al-'Uyun (4:155).
Ibn Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar (4): 33: 'If correction differs for two statements and one of them is the statement of the Imam or in the matn, the statement of the Imam is taken because he is the founder of the madhhab, and what is in the matn because they are established for transmitting the madhhab.' And he said in it (1:489): 'Whenever tarjih differs, what is in the matn is given preponderance.' And he said in it (2): 299 also: 'Matn are given precedence over sharh.' And he said in it (1): 77 also: 'In (Qada' al-Fawa'it) from al-Bahr, that if correction and fatwa conflict, acting upon what agrees with the matn is more appropriate.' End. And likewise if one of them is in the sharh and the other in the fatawa, because they stated that what is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa. But this is when there is explicit correction of each of the two statements or no correction at all. As for if the matter of the matn is mentioned without explicit correction but the opposite is explicitly corrected, then al-Allama Qasim indicated giving preponderance to the second because it is explicit correction, and what is in the matn is implicit correction, and explicit correction takes precedence over implicit correction: meaning the matn's obligation to mention what is correct in the madhhab. And likewise there is no choice if one is the statement of the Imam and the other is the statement of someone else, because when the two corrections conflict they cancel each other out, so we revert to the principle of giving precedence to the statement of the Imam. Rather, in 'Shahadat' of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya: 'It is established with us that no fatwa or action is taken except according to the statement of the Great Imam, and it is not deviated from to their statement or the statement of one of them or others except for necessity like the case of muzara'ah, even if the scholars state that the fatwa is on their statement, because he is the founder of the madhhab and the most advanced Imam.' End. And similar is in al-Bahr when discussing the times of prayer, and in it from the Book of Qada': 'It is permissible to give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam, rather it is obligatory even if one does not know from where he said.' End. Ibn Nujaym said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (6): 310: 'The operative ruling is what is in the matn, because if what is in the matn and the fatawa conflict, the relied-upon is what is in the matn. And likewise what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa.' And he said in it (3): 142: 'Giving fatwa according to what is in the matn is more appropriate.' Al-Haskafi said in al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1): 341: 'Giving fatwa according to what is in the matn is more appropriate.' And he said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar (5): 452: 'It is given preponderance in al-Shurunbulaliyya that what is in the matn and sharh is more appropriate than what is in the books of fatawa, so let it be memorized.'
Al-Timirtashi said in Manh al-Ghaffar (3107/2/b): 'If correction differs, the relied-upon is what is in the matn.'

Commentary
This is a methodological discussion from the Hanafi fiqh tradition concerning the hierarchy of textual sources when conflicts arise in legal rulings. The passage establishes a clear principle: texts found in the core matn (such as al-Hidayah, al-Quduri) take precedence over those in sharh (commentaries), and sharh take precedence over fatawa (fatwa collections). This hierarchy is supported by quotations from major Hanafi authorities including al-Shurunbulali, al-Hamawi, al-Tartusi, Ibn Abidin, Ibn Nujaym, al-Haskafi, and al-Timirtashi.

The key nuance is that this precedence applies only when there is no explicit tashih (declaration of correctness) in the lower tier. If a sharh or fatwa collection explicitly states that a particular ruling is sahih, asahh, or that the fatwa is upon it, that explicit correction overrides the implicit correctness of the matn. This is because the matn's correctness is deemed 'iltizami' (implicit, by virtue of the matn's purpose to transmit the correct madhhab position), while a direct tashih is 'sarihi' (explicit). Explicit correction takes priority.

Additionally, if both corrections conflict, or if one is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa and the other of his students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the Imam's saying is given precedence because he is the founder of the madhhab. However, later scholars note that this rule is relaxed in cases of necessity, such as the issue of muzara'ah (sharecropping), where the fatwa is on the saying of the two students.

Ibn Abidin and others emphasize that this hierarchy is foundational. The passage concludes by citing al-Lakhnawi, who lists explicit phrases that constitute tashih sarih (explicit correction): 'this is sahih', 'asahh', 'upon it is the fatwa', 'by it fatwa is given', 'by it we take', etc.

In practice, this means a mufti or student should first consult the matn. If the ruling is not found there, or if there is a conflict, they should then consult the sharh, and finally fatawa collections. But if a lower-tier source explicitly corrects a ruling, that takes precedence over the matn's default position.

Key Terms
تصحيح صريحي (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥī): Explicit correction: a clear statement in a sharh or fatwa that a particular ruling is correct, using phrases like 'sahih', 'asahh', 'upon it is the fatwa', etc.
تصحيح التزامي (taṣḥīḥ iltizāmī): Implicit correction: the inherent assumption that a matn contains the correct madhhab position, without explicit declaration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a sharh to override a matn according to the Hanafi methodology?
A) Any statement in the sharh that differs from the matn
B) The sharh must explicitly declare the ruling as 'sahih', 'asahh', or similar
C) The sharh must be authored by a later scholar
D) The matn must not mention the issue

Key Takeaway
Explicit tashih in a lower source can override the matn, and the Imam's statement is supreme unless necessity dictates otherwise.

6 min
Precedence Among Hanafi Texts: Matn, Sharh, Fatwa
Establishes hierarchy of authority among Hanafi fiqh works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of fiqh sources to resolve conflicting rulings and identify when an explicit correction overrides the default precedence.

Core Idea
Matn rules supreme until a lower text explicitly corrects it.

When studying Hanafi fiqh, you will often encounter different rulings in different books. How do you decide which one to follow? This lesson explains the classic hierarchy: matn (core texts) take precedence over sharh (commentaries), and sharh over fatawa (fatwa collections). However, there is a crucial exception: if a lower text contains an explicit statement that a particular ruling is correct, that explicit correction overrides the default order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual layers
Determine which texts in your reference are matn (e.g., al-Quduri, Kanz al-Daqaiq), sharh (e.g., al-Hidayah), or fatwa collections (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya).
Matn are composed for transmitting the madhhab; sharh explain; fatawa record practical outcomes.
2
Apply the default hierarchy
If no explicit correction is present, take the ruling from the highest layer: matn > sharh > fatwa.
The default assumes the matn's author committed to include only the correct view.
3
Check for explicit correction
Look in lower layers (sharh or fatwa) for phrases like 'alayhi al-fatwa', 'al-sahih', 'bihi na'khudh', which indicate an explicit preference.
Explicit correction must be clearly stated; mere discussion of a view is not enough.
4
Override if explicit
If an explicit correction is found in a lower layer, that ruling takes precedence over the higher layer's implicit stance.
Explicit correction (tasrih sarih) is stronger than the implicit commitment (tasrih iltizami) of matn authors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن ما في المتون مقدم على ما في الشروح وما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى ، فإذا وجدت مسألة في المتون الموضوعة لنقل المذهب ووجد خلافُها في الشروح أُخِذَ بما في المتون، وإذا وقعت المخالفة بين ما في الشروح وبين ما في الفتوى ، أُخِذَ بما في الشروح لكن هذا إذا لم يوجد التصحيح الصريحي في الطبقة التحتانية.
(1) قال الشيخ أمين) مؤلف ردّ المحتار على الدر المختار» في «تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية» في «كتاب الإجارة»: «ذكر ابنُ وَهْبان (3) وغيره : إنه لا عبرة لما يقوله في «القنية) إذا خالف غيره، وقالوا أيضاً : إنَّ ما في المتون مقدم على ما في الشروح، وما في الشروح على ما في الفتاوى». انتهى
(0) وقال اللكنوي أيضاً في «التعليقات السنية (ص180): «ما في المتون مقدم على ما في الشروح ، وما في الشروح مقدم على ما في الفتاوى..... (1) بأن يكون صرّح في الشرح أو الفتاوى بأنه هذا القول صحيح ، أو أصح، أو عليه الفتوى، أو به يفتى، أو به نأخذ ، أو غيرها من الألفاظ الصريحة في ترجيح هذا القول مما نصت عليها في كتب رسم المفتي، وتمام هذا البحث في المدخل»(ص245 - 249).
وقال أيضاً في «كتاب الفرائض» منه) : في مسألة ما إذا ترك الميت بنت عم وابن خال، بعدما ذكر عن الخير الرملي (3) أنه أفتى بأن الكل لبنت العم : «قد ذكروا أن ما في المتون مصحح التزاماً – أي التزم أصحاب المتون أن يذكروا فيها الصحيح -، وأنّ التصحيح الصريح أقوى من التصحيح الالتزامي " ومـا أفـتـى بـه الخـير الرملي صرّح بتصحيحه في «جامع المضمرات»، وقــول المؤلف : إنَّ المتون موضوعة لنقل المذهب ؛ لا يدلّ على ترجيح ما فيها من مسألتنا ;
Indeed, what is in the matn (primary texts) is given precedence over what is in the sharh (commentaries), and what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa (fatwa collections). So if a ruling is found in the matn—which are composed for transmitting the madhhab—and its contrary is found in the sharh, then what is in the matn is taken. And if a conflict occurs between what is in the sharh and what is in the fatwa, then what is in the sharh is taken. However, this is only when there is no explicit correction (tasrih sarih) in the lower layer.
(1) Shaykh Amin [Ibn Abidin], author of Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar, said in Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya, in the Book of Ijarah: 'Ibn Wahban and others mentioned that no consideration is given to what is said in al-Qunya if it contradicts others. They also said: Indeed, what is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa.' End quote.
(0) Al-Lakhnawi also said in al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyya (p. 180): 'What is in the matn is given precedence over what is in the sharh, and what is in the sharh is given precedence over what is in the fatawa...' (1) Provided that it is explicitly stated in the sharh or the fatawa that this ruling is sahih (correct), or asahh (more correct), or 'alayhi al-fatwa (the fatwa is upon it), or bihi yafti (with it one gives fatwa), or bihi na'khudh (we take it), or other explicit expressions indicating the preference of this ruling, as mentioned in the books on the protocol of the mufti. The complete discussion of this topic is in al-Madkhal (pp. 245-249).
He also said in the Book of Fara'id therein: Concerning the case where the deceased leaves a paternal cousin (bint 'amm) and a maternal cousin (ibn khal), after mentioning that al-Khayr al-Ramli gave a fatwa that the entire estate goes to the paternal cousin: 'They have mentioned that what is in the matn is implicitly corrected (musahhah iltizaman)—meaning that the authors of the matn committed themselves to mention the correct ruling—and that explicit correction (tasrih sarih) is stronger than implicit correction (tasrih iltizami). And what al-Khayr al-Ramli gave as a fatwa is explicitly corrected in Jami' al-Mudammarat. And the author's statement that the matn are composed for transmitting the madhhab does not indicate the preference of what is in them concerning our case.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule from the Hanafi school regarding the hierarchy of authority among different layers of fiqh literature. The principle stated is: matn (core texts like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, Kanz al-Daqaiq, etc.) take precedence over sharh (commentaries like al-Hidayah, al-Inayah, etc.), which in turn take precedence over fatawa (later fatwa collections like al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya, etc.). The reasoning is that matn authors deliberately include only the soundest (asahh) or most relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions of the madhhab, making them the most authoritative. Commentaries may discuss weaker views, and fatwa collections may record practical concessions. However, there is an important exception: if a lower-layer text (sharh or fatwa) contains an explicit correction (tasrih sarih)—such as stating 'this is the correct view' or 'the fatwa is upon this'—then that explicit correction overrides the default precedence, because the higher-layer text's authority is only implicit (tasrih iltizami) and weaker than an explicit statement. The passage quotes Ibn Abidin and al-Lakhnawi to support this principle, and illustrates it with a fara'id case where a fatwa from al-Khayr al-Ramli, explicitly endorsed in Jami' al-Mudammarat, is preferred over the matn's implicit stance.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutun): Primary Hanafi fiqh texts that transmit the soundest positions of the madhhab, e.g., al-Mukhtar, Kanz al-Daqaiq, al-Quduri.
الشروح (al-shuruh): Commentaries on the matn that explain and may discuss competing positions.
الفتاوى (al-fatawa): Later collections of fatwas that record practical rulings, often for specific contexts.
التصحيح الصريحي (al-tasrih al-sarihi): An explicit statement in a sharh or fatwa that a particular ruling is correct, e.g., 'alayhi al-fatwa.'
التصحيح الالتزامي (al-tasrih al-iltizami): The implicit commitment by matn authors to include only the correct ruling in their texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi hierarchy of fiqh sources, what happens when a matn and a sharh conflict, and the sharh does NOT contain an explicit correction (tasrih sarih)?
A) The sharh is taken because it is more detailed.
B) The matn is taken because matn have implicit authority.
C) The fatwa is taken because it is later.
D) The mufti must exercise ijtihad independently.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy of texts (matn > sharh > fatwa) is a default rule that is overridden only by explicit corrections in lower-layer works.

The Canonical Hanafi Texts: The Three and Four Mutoon
Defining the most relied-upon matn works and their authors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three canonical Hanafi mutoon and explain why they are considered the most authoritative.

Core Idea
Hanafi mutoon are not all texts; only those by leading imams are the foundation.

In the Hanafi school, when scholars say 'what is in the mutoon takes precedence,' they refer to a select group of concise texts. This lesson clarifies which texts are meant and why they hold such authority. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for navigating Hanafi legal references.

Guided Path
1
Define 'mutoon' in the Hanafi context
Understand that mutoon refers to specific concise texts authored by highly reliable scholars, not any summary.
2
List the five primary mutoon
The passage mentions al-Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Mukhtar, Majma' al-Bahrayn, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
3
Identify the three mutoon
The most relied upon are al-Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
4
Explain the four mutoon
When 'four mutoon' is used, it includes one of the additional two: al-Mukhtar or Majma' al-Bahrayn.
5
Recognize the authors' credentials
The authority of these texts stems from the eminence and reliability of their authors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المراد بالمتون في قولهم : ما في المتون مقدم، ليس جميع المتون ، بل المختصرات التي ألفها حداق الأئمة، وكبار الفقهاء المعروفين بالعلم والزهد والفقه والثقة في الرواية، كأبي جعفر الطحاوي والكَرْخي والحاكم الشهيد والقُدُوري، ومن في هذه الطبقة. وقد كثر اعتماد المتأخرين على «الوقاية لبرهان الشريعة، و«كنز الدقائق» لأبي البركات حافظ الدين عبد الله بن أحمد النَّسَفِي ، المتوفى سنة عشرة وسبعمئة ، و«المختار» لأبي الفضل مجد الدين عبد الله بن محمود الموصلي، المتوفى سنة ثلاث وثمانين وستمئة ، ومجمع «البحرين» المظفر الدين أحمد بن علي البغدادي المتوفى سنة أربع وتسعين وستمئة، و«مختصر القدوري لأحمد بن محمد المتوفى سنة ثمان وعشرين وأربعمئة ؛ وذلك لما علموا من جلالة مؤلّفيها ، والتزامهم إيراد مسائل معتمد عليها. وأشهرها ذكراً، وأقواها اعتماداً: «الوقاية»، و«الكنز»، و«مختصر القدوري»، وهي المراد بقولهم : المتون الثلاثة، وإذا أطلقوا المتون الأربعة أرادوا هذه الثلاثة : و«المختار»، أو «المجمع».
Then what is meant by 'mutoon' in their statement 'what is in the mutoon takes precedence' is not all mutoon, but rather the summaries authored by the leading imams and the senior jurists known for knowledge, asceticism, fiqh, and reliability in transmission, like Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, al-Hakim al-Shahid, and al-Quduri, and those of this class. The later scholars have heavily relied upon al-Wiqayah by Burhan al-Shari'ah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Abu al-Barakat Hafiz al-Din Abdullah ibn Ahmad al-Nasafi (d. 710 AH), al-Mukhtar by Abu al-Fadl Majd al-Din Abdullah ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili (d. 683 AH), Majma' al-Bahrayn by Muzafar al-Din Ahmad ibn Ali al-Baghdadi (d. 694 AH), and Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ahmad ibn Muhammad (d. 428 AH); that is because of their knowledge of the eminence of their authors and their commitment to presenting relied-upon issues. The most famous in mention and strongest in reliance are al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and these are what is meant by the 'three mutoon'. And if they use 'the four mutoon', they mean these three plus al-Mukhtar or Majma' al-Bahrayn.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'mutoon' in the Hanafi context. It clarifies that when scholars say 'what is in the mutoon takes precedence', they are not referring to all summaries, but only to those authored by the most reliable jurists, specifically those from the early period like al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, al-Hakim al-Shahid, and al-Quduri. The later scholars particularly relied on five works: al-Wiqayah by Burhan al-Shari'ah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Nasafi, al-Mukhtar by al-Mawsili, Majma' al-Bahrayn by al-Baghdadi, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Quduri. Among these, the three most relied upon are al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri, forming the 'three mutoon'. When 'four mutoon' is mentioned, it includes either al-Mukhtar or Majma' al-Bahrayn in addition. These texts are considered authoritative because of the authors' eminence and their commitment to only including reliable, operative rulings.

Key Terms
المتون الثلاثة (al-mutoon al-thalatha): The three most authoritative Hanafi concise texts: al-Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
المتون الأربعة (al-mutoon al-arba'a): The three mutoon plus either al-Mukhtar or Majma' al-Bahrayn.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Al-Wiqayah, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and Majma' al-Bahrayn
D) Al-Mukhtar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi three mutoon are al-Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Mukhtasar al-Quduri; they are the most authoritative concise texts due to their authors' eminence and reliability.

Prohibition of Issuing Fatwa from Unreliable Books
Ruling on prohibited sources for ifta'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of prohibited books for issuing fatwa according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling to evaluate a given book's sufficiency.

Core Idea
Issuing fatwa from a book that lacks comprehensiveness or reliable source verification is prohibited (haram).

The authority to issue fatwa is a serious responsibility. This passage from 'Radd al-Muhtar' by Ibn Abidin establishes a crucial principle: a mufti cannot rely on just any fiqh book. We will learn which types of books are insufficient and why, so that you can appreciate the need for rigorous source verification in issuing legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the overall ruling
Identify that the passage states 'la yajuz al-ifta' (issuing fatwa is not permissible). Determine the hukm level: it is haram because of the serious risk of misrepresenting the Shariah.
The phrase 'la yajuz' in Hanafi fiqh indicates prohibition.
2
List the three categories of prohibited books
Extract from the passage: (1) summarized books (almukhtasarah) like 'al-Nahr', 'Sharh al-Kanz' by al-Ayni, and 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar'; (2) books whose authors are unknown or unreliable, like 'Sharh al-Kanz' by Mulla Miskin and 'Sharh al-Niqayah' by al-Quhistani; (3) books containing weak narrations, like 'al-Qunyah' by al-Zahidi.
Each category has a distinct reason: omission of detail, lack of trust in author, or inclusion of weak material.
3
Understand the exception
The passage notes an exception: fatwa from such books is permissible if the mufti knows the original source and takes the ruling from that source. This implies the book can be used as a pointer but not as independent evidence.
The exception is narrow and requires direct knowledge of the transmitted ruling.
4
Apply the principle to similar works
The author adds 'al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair' by Ibn Nujaym to the list due to its extreme conciseness, which can mislead without consulting commentaries. Consider whether other concise works would fall under this prohibition.
The criterion is not just length but whether the work omits essential context and proofs.
5
Connect to the universal principle from Ali al-Qari
Ali al-Qari states that transmission of hadith, fiqh, and tafsir is only allowed from widely circulated (mutadawalah) books due to risk of forgery. This reinforces the rule: fatwa must come from reliable, verified sources.
This principle is a key methodological safeguard in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة
الدراسة الرابعة
في فوائد متفرقة مفيدة للمفتي والمصنّف
• قال في «رد المحتار» نقلاً عن «شرح الأشباه» للشيخ هبة الله البَعْلِي)، قال شيخنا العلامة صالح: لا يجوز الإفتاء:
١. من الكتب المختصرة، كـ «النهر» (لعمر بن إبراهيم بن محمد المشهور بابن نُجَيْم المصري الحنفي، سراج الدين، أخو صاحب «البحر الرائق»، من مؤلفاته: «النهر الفائق بشرح الكنز دقائق»، و«إجابة السائل باختصار أنفع الوسائل»، و«عقد الجواهر في الكلام على سورة الكوثر»، (ت ١٠٠٥هـ).) ، و «شرح الكنز» للعيني (وهو محمود بن أحمد بن موسى العنتابي العيني الحلبي القاهري الحنفي، أبو محمد، بدر الدين، قال السيوطي: كان إماماً عالماً علامة عارفاً بالعربية والتصريف حافظاً للغة. من مؤلفاته: «البناية في شرح الهداية»، و«رمز الحقائق شرح كنز الدقائق»، و«عمدة القاري شرح صحيح البُخَارِي» (٧٦٢ - ٨٥٥هـ).)، و«الدر المختار شرح تنوير الأبصار».
٢. أو لعدم الاطلاع على حال مصنفيها، كـ«شرح الكنز» لملا مسكين (وهو معين الدين الهروي المعروف بملاً مسكين من مؤلفاته: «شرح الكنز»، (ت٩٥٤هـ).)، و«شرح النقاية» للقُهُسْتانِي (وهو مُحَمَّدُ الخُرَاسَانِي القُهستاني، شمس الدين، المفتي ببخارا، من مؤلفاته: «جامع الرموز في شرح النقاية»، قال الإمام اللكنوي: هو من الكتب الغير معتبرة لعدم الاعتماد على مؤلفه).
. أو لنقل الأقوال الضعيفة فيها، كـ«القُنْية» للزَّاهِدِي، فلا يجوز الإفتاء من هذه إلا إذا علم المنقولَ عنه وأَخْذَه منه (وتكملة العبارة: هكذا سمعته منه، وهو علامة في الفقه مشهور والعهدة عليه. ينظر: «رد المحتار» (١: ٤٨).). انتهى
ثم قال: وينبغي إلحاق «الأشباه والنظائر» (لإبراهيم بن محمد ابن نُجَيْم المصري زين العابدين من مؤلفاته: «البحر الرائق شرح كنز الدقائق»، و«الرسائل الزينية»، و«الأشباه والنظائر»، و«فتح الغفار شرح المنار»، قال الإمام اللكنوي عن مؤلفاته: كلها حسنةٌ جداً، (٩٢٦ - ٩٧٠هـ).) بها، فإنّ فيها من الإيجاز في التعبير ما لا يفهم معناه إلا بعد الاطلاع على مأخذه، بل فيها في مواضع كثيرة الإيجاز المخلّ يظهرُ ذلك من مارس مطالعتها مع الحواشي، فلا يأمنُ المفتي من الوقوع في الغلط إذا اقتصر عليها، فلا بد له من مراجعة ما كتب عليها من الحواشي أو غيرها. انتهى
وفي «تذكرة الموضوعات» (الاسم المطبوع به هو الأسرار المرفوعة في الأحاديث الموضوعة، وهناك اختلاف في اسمه. ينظر للوقوف عليه: الأسرار (ص ١٥ - ١٧)، و(المصنوع (ص١٤).) لعلي القاري المكي (وهو علي بن سلطان محمد الهروي القَارِيِّ الحنفي، أبو الحسن، نور الدين، من مؤلفاته: «فتح باب العناية بشرح النقاية»، و «مرقاة المفاتيح شرح مشكاة المصابيح»، و«الأثمار الجنية في طبقات الحنفية»، و«شرح مسند الإمام»، (٩٣٠ - ١٠١٤هـ).): «من القواعد الكلية أن نقل الأحاديث النبوية، والمسائل الفقهيّة، والتفاسير القرآنية، لا يجوز إلا من الكتب المتداولة؛ لعدم الاعتماد على غيرها من وضع الزنادقة، وإلحاق الملاحدة».
وقال علي القاري المكي في بعض رسائله: قال عصام الدين في حقِّ القُهُسْتانِي: إِنَّهُ لم يكن من تلامذة شيخ الإسلام الهروي، لا من أعاليهم، ولا من أدانيهم، وإنما كان دلال الكتب في زمانه، ولا كان يعرف الفقه، ولا غيره بين أقرانه، ويؤيده أنه يجمع في شرحه هذا بين الغث والسمين، والصحيح والضعيف من غير تصحيح ولا تدقيق، فهو كحاطب الليل، جامع بين الرطب واليابس في الليل. (ت) نحو: ٩٥٣هـ).
A benefit. The fourth study: in scattered benefits useful for the mufti and the author. He said in 'Radd al-Muhtar' quoting from 'Sharh al-Ashbah' by Shaykh Hibah Allah al-Ba'li: Our teacher, the scholar Salih, said: Issuing fatwa is not permissible: 1. From summarized books, such as 'al-Nahr', 'Sharh al-Kanz' by al-Ayni, and 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar Sharh Tanwir al-Absar'. 2. Or due to lack of knowledge of the state of their authors, such as 'Sharh al-Kanz' by Mulla Miskin and 'Sharh al-Niqayah' by al-Quhistani. 3. Or due to transmission of weak statements in them, such as 'al-Qunyah' by al-Zahidi. So issuing fatwa from these is not permissible unless one knows what is transmitted and takes it from him. End. Then he said: And it is appropriate to add 'al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair' to them, for indeed in it there is such conciseness in expression that its meaning is not understood except after reviewing its sources; rather in many places there is damaging conciseness that appears to one who practices studying it with commentaries. The mufti is not safe from falling into error if he confines himself to it, so he must review what has been written on it of commentaries or other works. End. And in 'Tadhkirat al-Mawdu'at' by Ali al-Qari al-Makki: 'It is among the universal principles that transmission of prophetic hadiths, fiqh issues, and Quranic exegesis is not permissible except from widely circulated books, because there is no reliance on others due to the fabrications of heretics and insertions of atheists.' And Ali al-Qari al-Makki said in some of his treatises: Isam al-Din said about al-Quhistani: He was not among the students of Shaykh al-Islam al-Harawi, neither from their highest nor their lowest; rather he was a book dealer in his time, and he did not know fiqh nor anything else among his peers. What supports this is that he compiled in his commentary the worthless and the valuable, the authentic and the weak, without verification or precision; he is like a gatherer of firewood at night, collecting dry and wet in the dark.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a methodological ruling about the condition for issuing fatwa. It states that a mufti cannot rely on certain types of books: first, summarized books that omit details and proofs (like 'al-Nahr' by Ibn Nujaym, 'Sharh al-Kanz' by al-Ayni, and 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' by al-Haskafi); second, books whose authors are unknown in reliability (like 'Sharh al-Kanz' by Mulla Miskin and 'Sharh al-Niqayah' by al-Quhistani); third, books that contain weak or unacceptable narrations (like 'al-Qunyah' by al-Zahidi). Exception is made if the mufti knows the original source of the transmitted content. The author then adds 'al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair' by Ibn Nujaym to this list because its extreme conciseness can mislead without consulting commentaries. The passage further quotes Ali al-Qari al-Makki's universal principle that only widely circulated books should be relied upon for hadith, fiqh, and tafsir due to risk of forgery. The final quote about al-Quhistani confirms the unreliability of his commentary for fatwa.

Key Terms
الكتب المختصرة (al-kutub al-mukhtasarah): Summarized books that omit detailed proofs and conditions, making them insufficient for issuing fatwa without referring to fuller commentaries.
الإفتاء (al-ifta'): Issuing a legal ruling (fatwa) on a matter of Islamic law. It is a serious responsibility requiring thorough knowledge.
الكتب المتداولة (al-kutub al-mutadawalah): Widely circulated and accepted books among scholars, free from corruption and unreliable additions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a reason for prohibiting fatwa from a book?
A) The book is summarized and omits essential details.
B) The author's reliability is unknown.
C) The book contains weak narrations.
D) The book is written in a difficult language.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only issue fatwa from books that are both comprehensive and verified as reliable; summarizing or unknown authorship renders a book insufficient for independent fatwa.

The Obligation to Use Only Reliable Books for Fatwa
Warnings about using unreliable books for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using unreliable books for fatwa and identify which books are unreliable according to the text.

Core Idea
Fatwa must only be taken from widely circulated, verified books; unreliable books like al-Qunyah are impermissible.

In this passage, the author lays down a critical methodological rule for muftis: not all fiqh books are equal. Some contain weak or fabricated opinions, others are too concise and misleading without commentary. The Hanafi tradition insists on using only widely transmitted books (al-kutub al-mutadawila) to preserve the integrity of legal rulings. Let us unpack the specific warnings and the general principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving fatwa from books that are not widely circulated or that contain weak opinions. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram) unless one knows the original source and has taken it from there.
2
Recognize the specific books cited as unreliable
Two books are explicitly mentioned: al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi, which contains many weak opinions, and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, which is too concise and can mislead if used without commentaries.
Al-Ashbah is not outright prohibited but strongly cautioned against.
3
Understand the rationale
The rationale is that unreliable books may have been tampered with by heretics, or their brevity hides underlying assumptions, leading to errors in fatwa.
4
Apply the general principle
Ali al-Qari states a universal rule: transmission of hadith, fiqh, and tafsir is only allowed from widely circulated books (al-kutub al-mutadawila) because their copies are numerous and correct.
This principle applies to both text transmission and fatwa derivation.
5
Note the additional caution for concise works
Even well-known works like al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir require consultation of commentaries to avoid harmful brevity.
The mufti must not rely solely on the matn without the sharh.

Source Text

Or for transmitting weak opinions from it, like al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi, so it is not permissible to give fatwa from these unless one knows what is transmitted from him and has taken it from him. End. Then he said: It is should also to include al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir among them, for in it there is such brevity in expression that its meaning is not understood except after examining its source, rather in many places there is harmful brevity; that becomes apparent to one who practices studying it with marginal commentaries, so the mufti is not safe from falling into error if he confines himself to it, so he must review what is written on it by way of marginalia or other works. End. And in Tadhkirat al-Mawdu'at of Ali al-Qari al-Makki: 'Among the universal principles is that the transmission of prophetic hadiths, juristic issues, and Quranic interpretations is not permissible except from widely circulated books, due to lack of reliance on other books that may be from the fabrication of heretics and the insertions of atheists, unlike preserved books, whose copies are numerous and correct.' End. And Ali al-Qari al-Makki said in some of his epistles: Isam al-Din said concerning al-Qahustani: 'He was not among the students of Shaykh al-Islam al-Harawi, neither among their high nor low, rather he was a bookseller in his time, and he did not know fiqh nor other things among his peers, and supporting that is that he compiled in this commentary of his between the bad and the good, and the sound and the weak, without correction or verification, so he is like one gathering firewood at night, collecting dry and wet in the dark.'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the sources a mufti may rely upon. It begins by warning against using books that contain weak opinions, like al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi, stating that it is impermissible to issue fatwa from such books unless one knows the original transmission source. The author then includes al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir in the same caution due to its overly concise expressions that can mislead without consulting commentaries. Next, Ali al-Qari quotes a general principle: transmission of hadith, fiqh, and tafsir is only allowed from widely circulated books (al-kutub al-mutadawila), because other books may have been tampered with by heretics. Finally, a criticism of al-Qahustani is related, pointing out that his commentary mixed sound and weak materials without verification, resembling a night wood-gatherer. The lesson emphasizes the necessity of using only verified, widely transmitted sources for fatwa.

Key Terms
الكتب المتداولة (al-kutub al-mutadawila): Books that are widely circulated, with multiple accurate copies, and commonly used among scholars.
القُنْية (al-Qunyah): A book by al-Zahidi containing many weak and unreliable opinions; not a primary source for fatwa.
الأشباه والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir): A concise work by Ibn Nujaym that requires clarification through commentaries; using it alone for fatwa is risky.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only use widely circulated, verified books for fatwa, and must consult commentaries when using concise works like al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Identifying Unreliable Books in Hanafi Fatwa
Listing books considered unreliable for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which books are considered unreliable for fatwa in the Hanafi school and state the methodological principle that governs their rejection.

Core Idea
Not all Hanafi books are authoritative for fatwa — only those that align with the established principles of the school.

A mufti must know which sources are reliable for issuing fatwas. This lesson introduces several books that Hanafi scholars have deemed unreliable, along with the reasoning behind their exclusion. Understanding this will protect you from basing rulings on weak or unaccepted material.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the passage lists 'unreliable books' (al-kutub ghayr al-mu'tabara) — works that should not be used as primary sources for fatwa without verification.
2
Note the specific books
Read the names of the books and their authors: Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi, works of al-Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, Mushtamil al-Ahkam, al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya.
Each of these books has a reason for being considered unreliable, such as containing weak narrations or contradicting established rules.
3
Understand the methodological principle
The passage cites the principle: 'The transmission of al-Zahidi does not contradict the reliable Hanafi transmissions.' This means that isolated or weak narratives do not outweigh the well-established sources (mu'tabarat).
4
Apply the criterion
For each book, consider whether its content aligns with the principles of the Hanafi school. If not, it should be avoided unless supported by other reliable sources.
For example, al-Hawi by al-Zahidi is 'famous for transmitting weak reports', so it is not authoritative.
5
Recognize the practical importance
A mufti must check the reliability of a source before issuing a fatwa. Using an unreliable book can lead to incorrect rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة الرابعة فوائد متفرقة للمفتي

كان يعرف بالفقه وغيره بين أقرانه، ويؤيده أنه يجمعُ في «شرحه» هذا بين الغث والسمين، والصحيح والضعيف من غير تحقيق وتدقيق، فهو كحاطب الليل، الجامع بين الرطب واليابس في الليل». انتهى.

٢. ومن الكتب الغير المعتبرة : فتاوى إبراهيم شاهي» من مؤلفات القاضي شهاب الدين الدولة آبادي) ، كما نقله عبد القادر البدايوني" في «منتخب التواريخ» أستاذه العلامة ، أجلّ علماء العهد الأكبري الشيخ حاتم السنبهلي(۳)، المتوفى سنة ثمان وستين بعد تسعمئة.

Fourth study: Miscellaneous benefits for the mufti

He was known for fiqh and other sciences among his peers, and it is supported that he compiled in this 'Sharh' the fat and lean, the correct and weak without verification and scrutiny, so he is like a firewood gatherer at night, collecting wet and dry in the dark." End.

2. Among the unreliable books: 'Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi' from the works of Qadi Shihab al-Din al-Dawlatabadi, as quoted by 'Abd al-Qadir al-Bada'uni in 'Muntakhab al-Tawarikh' from his teacher, the eminent scholar of the Akbari era, Shayk Hatim al-Sannahbali, who died in 968 AH.

Among them: the works of Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad al-Zahidi, a Mu'tazili in belief, Hanafi in branches, died 656 AH, such as 'al-Qunyah', 'al-Hawi', 'al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri', 'Zad al-A'immah', and others. For it was said in 'Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamdiyya': 'The transmission of al-Zahidi does not contradict the reliable transmissions of the Hanafiyya, for Ibn Wahban mentioned: One does not pay attention to what the author of 'al-Qunyah' transmitted contrary to the rules, unless supported by transmission from another source.' The same is in 'al-Nahr'. End. And in another place: 'Al-Hawi by al-Zahidi is famous for transmitting weak reports.' End.

. Among them: 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' from the works of Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali al-Hadadi, died 800 AH, as quoted by the author of 'Kashf al-Zunun' from Mawla al-Birkili.

. Among them: 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam' by Fakhr al-Din al-Rumi, as quoted by the author of 'Kashf' also from al-Birkili.

. Among them: 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya' by Fadlallah ibn Muhammad ibn Ayyub, student of 'Jami' al-Mudammarat', as quoted by the author of 'Kashf' from al-Birkili that he said: 'They are not from the reliable books, so it is not permissible to act upon what is in them unless it is known to be in agreement with the principles.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is from the author's introduction to the fourth study, which provides miscellaneous benefits for the mufti. Here, the author lists several books that are not considered reliable for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school. The first part criticizes a certain scholar's commentary for mixing weak and strong material. Then, specific unreliable books are named: 'Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi' by Qadi Shihab al-Din al-Dawlatabadi, cited by al-Bada'uni from his teacher. Next are the works of al-Zahidi, who was Mu'tazili in 'aqida, such as 'al-Qunyah' and 'al-Hawi'. Ibn Wahban and the author of 'Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamdiyya' state that al-Zahidi's transmissions do not outweigh the reliable Hanafi sources, and his 'al-Hawi' is known for weak narrations. Also listed is 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' by al-Hadadi, and 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam' by al-Rumi, as reported by al-Birkili. Finally, 'al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya' by Fadlallah ibn Ayyub is deemed unreliable unless it matches established principles. The mufti must be aware of these so as not to base rulings on weak compilations.

Key Terms
الكتب الغير المعتبرة (al-kutub ghayr al-mu'tabara): Books that are not considered authoritative for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
نقل الزاهدي لا يعارض نقل المعتبرات النعمانية (naql al-Zahidi la yu'arid naql al-mu'tabarat al-nu'maniyya): The transmissions of al-Zahidi do not contradict the reliable Hanafi transmissions (those of Abu Hanifa's school).

Evaluating Treatise Reliability and the Ruling on Takbir al-Tahrimah
Defense of a treatise's reliability and clarification of intra-Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for evaluating a fiqh treatise's reliability, state the Hanafi positions on the status of takbir al-tahrimah (Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf), and explain how to use a treatise with known weak points.

Core Idea
Even a treatise with some weak points can be valuable if the user knows the relied-upon positions.

A fiqh treatise's authority depends not only on its author but on the verification of its content. In this passage, the author defends Khulasat al-Kaidani against criticism, acknowledging two specific issues: the definition of wajib and the classification of takbir al-tahrimah. Understanding this defense requires grasping the intra-Hanafi dispute over takbir and the proper method for assessing a text's reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main criticisms against Khulasat al-Kaidani
From the passage, note that critics say the treatise mixes reliable and weak content ("dry and wet") and that its author may lack verification skills.
The author acknowledges these criticisms but argues the treatise is still beneficial.
2
Analyze the first criticism: the definition of wajib
The author of Khulasah defined wajib as 'that which is established by evidence containing ambiguity'—this is the standard usul definition. The critic (al-Laknawi) paired this with the listing of takbir as a wajib, implying inconsistency. The author argues that no pairing was intended.
The definition of wajib itself is not disputed; the dispute is about its application to takbir.
3
Analyze the second criticism: takbir al-tahrimah as wajib
Most reliable Hanafi books say takbir is sunnah or condition. But the author clarifies: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is wajib; according to Abu Yusuf, it is a condition. The treatise followed Abu Hanifa's view, which is the mufta bihi.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa (wajib) vs Abu Yusuf (condition).
4
Examine the third issue: sujud al-sahw for leaving tuma'nina
The treatise stated that sujud al-sahw is not obligatory for leaving tuma'nina, but the relied-upon position is that it is wajib. The author concedes this is an error in the treatise.
This is a mistake that the user must be aware of when using the treatise.
5
Conclude: how to use the treatise despite its issues
The author advises that if a teacher is mindful of these two issues (takbir ruling and sujud al-sahw), the treatise can still be highly beneficial due to its conciseness and wealth of useful content.
The lesson: a book is not useless because of a few errors; it requires informed use.

الطلبة، نفعنا الله تعالى بها. (۱) في «خلاصة الكيداني»(ق١ /أ).
(٢) أي أنه لا يلزم اعتقاد حقيته ؛ لثبوته بدليل ظني ، ومبنى الاعتقاد على اليقين، لكن يلزم العمل بموجبه للدلائل الدالة على وجوب اتباع الظنّ ، فجاحده لا يكفر، وتارك العمل به إن كان مؤولاً لا يفسق، ولا يضلل ؛ لأن التأويل في مظانه من سيرة السلف، وإلا فإن كان مستخفاً يضلل. ينظر: «التلويح و التوضيح ٢ : ٢٤٧ - ٢٤٨)، و«فتح الغفار (٢ : ٦٤) ، وسبيل الوصول» (ص۲۲۳).
فما بينه صاحب «الخلاصة» من حكم للواجب، فهو محل اتفاق، وهو في هذا المقام ذكر حكم الواجب كما نص عليه علماء الأصول، ولم يقصد به بيان حكم الواجب في الصلاة من أنه يجب عليه سجود سهو، وبذلك لا يُسلّم للإمام اللكنوي قـرنه بين تعريف صاحب الخلاصة» للواجب وحكمه وبين الواجبات في الصلاة، والله أعلم.
(۳) في «خلاصة الكيداني»(ق۱ /ب). (٤) أقول : لعل هذا سبق قلم من الإمام اللكنوي ؛ إذ أن الاتفاق في الكتب المعتبرة على أن التحريمة بكل ما فيه ذكر خالص الله من أسمائه شرط كالتهليل والتسمية ، وخص التحريمة بالتكبير فإنه واجب، ويكره تركه كراهية تحريم، وإنما السنة في التحريم هي رفع اليدين، وهذا عند الإمام أبي حنيفة له، وعند أبي يوسف الله فإن ذكر لفظ التكبير للتحريمة شرط لا تصح الصلاة إلا به. كما في منحة السلوك» (۱) : (۱۷۳) ، و«المراقي» (ص (۲۵۲)، و«نفحات السلوك» (ص٧٦)، و«تحفة الملوك» (ص (٧٦) ، و(اللباب (۱) : (۵۷) ، و (مختصر القدوري» (ص ٥٧»، ورد المحتار» و«الدر المختار (۱) : (۳۱۵) ، وحاشية الطحطاوي»(ص٢٥٢)، و«المشكاة»
And according to the first and second opinion, even if its author is among the reputable, for Ibn Kamal Pasha and Ibn Hamza are among the greatest of their era and the perfect of their time as we have detailed in 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya', yet its combining of dry and wet indicates its lack of reliability. For often the author is reputable in himself, but his book is not reputable due to his not adhering to criticism and refinement in it, and his collecting in it every dry and wet without verification and clarification. And that which proclaims at the highest call that it is an unreliable treatise, and that its author is either one without practice in issues and without knowledge of proofs, or one who did not commit to verification and refinement in it even if he is himself among those capable of tarjih, is reading this treatise from its beginning to its end, and examining its odd issues and unique rulings. For in it are issues contrary to zahir al-riwayah, contradictory to reliable books. Do you not see that he defined wajib in the beginning of his treatise as 'that which is established by evidence containing ambiguity', and mentioned that its ruling is like the ruling of fard in practice not in belief. Then in the second chapter, which is for explaining the obligatory acts of prayer, he included among the obligatory acts the wording of takbir for ihram. And this contradicts most reliable books, for they unanimously declare that the wording of takbir for ihram is sunnah, not wajib nor condition. As al-Laknawi will mention, and these issues others counted them among disliked acts. And he himself stated at the end of the chapter that the author of al-Muhit counted them among disliked acts. Perhaps this is a slip of pen and mind from him. And the commentators and scholars have followed up on him in this chapter. Similarly, the author stated that there is no obligation of sujud al-sahw for leaving tuma'nina in ruku' and sujud. And this contradicts the relied-upon position as I have pointed out in al-Marqat (pp. 41-42). So if one is mindful of these two matters in teaching it and taking from it, its benefit spreads and its knowledge becomes widespread, and it becomes safe from every defect and stain. I have studied it many times due to its extreme conciseness, precision of expression, and abundance of knowledge, which allows the teacher to teach it in one or two or three sessions depending on the level of the students before him. May Allah benefit us with it. (1) In 'Khulasat al-Kaidani' (folio 1/a). (2) That is, it is not necessary to believe in its truth because it is established by a conjectural proof, and belief is based on certainty. But it is necessary to act upon it due to the proofs indicating the obligation of following conjecture. So one who denies it does not become a disbeliever, and one who abandons action upon it, if he has a valid interpretation, is not sinful nor misguided, for interpretation in its proper place is from the conduct of the Salaf. Otherwise, if he belittles it, he is misguided. See: al-Talwih wa al-Tawdih 2:247-248, Fath al-Ghaffar 2:64, Sabil al-Wusul p.223. So what the author of al-Khulasah stated about the ruling of wajib is a matter of agreement. And in this context he mentioned the ruling of wajib as the usul scholars stated it. He did not intend by it to explain the ruling of wajib in prayer that it necessitates sujud al-sahw. Therefore, al-Laknawi's pairing between the definition of the author of al-Khulasah for wajib and its ruling and the obligatory acts in prayer is not conceded. And Allah knows best. (3) In 'Khulasat al-Kaidani' (folio 1/b). (4) I say: Perhaps this is a slip of pen from al-Laknawi. For there is consensus in the reliable books that the tahrimah (declaration of prohibition) with every word containing a pure mention of Allah's names is a condition, like tahlil and tasmiyah, and the specific tahrimah with takbir is wajib, and leaving it is disliked with tahrimi dislike. Rather, the sunnah in the tahrimah is raising the hands. This according to Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And according to Abu Yusuf, the wording of takbir for tahrimah is a condition without which the prayer is not valid. As in Minhat al-Suluk (1:173), al-Maraqi (p.252), Nafahat al-Suluk (p.76), Tuhfat al-Muluk (p.76), al-Lubab (1:57), Mukhtasar al-Quduri (p.57), Radd al-Muhtar and al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:315), Hashiyat al-Tahtawi (p.252), al-Mishkat.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a critical evaluation of the reliability of the treatise known as 'Khulasat al-Kaidani' (Summary of al-Kaidani). The author, writing in his work 'Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya', defends this treatise against criticisms that it mixes reliable and unreliable material. He acknowledges that some scholars have questioned its authority because its author included 'dry and wet'—meaning a mix of strong and weak content—without proper verification. However, the author argues that the treatise is still valuable and widely accepted, as evidenced by the numerous commentaries written upon it by prominent scholars such as Ibrahim al-Bukhari, Tashkubri Zada, al-Qahistani, and others. The author then addresses two specific criticisms raised by al-Laknawi. First, the definition of 'wajib' in the treatise: the author of al-Khulasah defined wajib as 'that which is established by evidence containing ambiguity,' which is the standard usul definition, and he did not intend to imply that wajib in prayer requires sujud al-sahw. Second, the listing of the wording of takbir al-tahrimah as a wajib act of prayer: the author notes that most reliable books consider it a sunnah or a condition, but he clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, uttering takbir for ihram is wajib, and leaving it is makruh tahrimi. Abu Yusuf considers it a condition. The third criticism about sujud al-sahw for leaving tuma'nina is acknowledged as incorrect—the author of al-Khulasah stated that it is not obligatory, but the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that it is obligatory. The passage concludes by advising that if one is aware of these two issues (the definition of wajib and the ruling on takbir, and the tuma'nina issue), the treatise can be taught and used beneficially.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): Defined as 'that which is established by evidence containing ambiguity' (ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة). Its ruling is like that of fard in practice but not in belief.
تكبيرة التحريمة (takbirat al-tahrimah): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' at the start of prayer, which prohibits worldly actions. In the treatise, it was listed as a wajib; but the commentator clarifies it is sunnah according to some, but according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness. The author of al-Khulasah said it is not obligatory for leaving tuma'nina, but the relied-upon position is that it is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view in the Hanafi school regarding the wording of takbir al-tahrimah?
A) It is a sunnah act.
B) It is a wajib act.
C) It is a condition (shart) for the validity of the prayer.
D) It is a pillar (rukn) of the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A fiqh treatise's authority is assessed by its content, not solely by its author's reputation; knowledge of intra-school disputes enables correct use of imperfect texts.
