Conditions for Using Non-Mu'tabar Books in Fatwa
List of conditions for deriving rulings from unreliable books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five conditions for using non-mu'tabar books and apply them to determine whether a ruling can be used for fatwa.

Core Idea
A ruling from an unreliable book is invalid if it contradicts reliable books or principles.

The Hanafi school maintains a clear hierarchy of authoritative books. Not every fiqh work can be used as a basis for fatwa. This lesson presents the five conditions set by Imam al-Lakhnawi for when a scholar may legitimately use a non-mu'tabar book. These safeguards prevent unverified rulings from entering the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope
Recognise that these conditions apply only to books that are not part of the mu'tabar (reliable) collection, such as al-Hidayah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Mu'tabar books are those from Zahir al-Riwayah and the later relied-upon texts.
2
Apply condition 1: check for contradiction
If a ruling in a non-mu'tabar book contradicts a ruling found in the reliable books, it must be rejected immediately.
Al-Lakhnawi said: 'If no trace in relied-upon books, do not dare to give fatwa with it.'
3
Apply condition 2: check for conformity to usul
Even if there is no direct contradiction, the ruling must align with the fundamental principles (usul) of the Hanafi school.
This ensures internal consistency of the madhhab.
4
Apply conditions 3-4: assess the scholar
Only a highly qualified scholar (ahliyyah) with extensive knowledge, precise reasoning, and strong memory may extract rulings from such books.
This prevents misuse by those lacking authority.
5
Apply condition 5: consult detailed works
The scholar must refer to the longer commentaries (shuruh), glosses (hawashi), and other detailed works to understand the full context and restrictions of the issue.
This ensures the ruling is not taken out of context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) فضوابط وشروط الأخذ من الكتب غير المعتبرة هي :
1. أن لا يخالف ما أخذه ما في الكتب المعتبرة، قال اللكنوي في النافع الكبير»(ص٢٦): «فإن وجد مسألة في كتاب لم يوجد لها أثر في الكتب المعتمدة، ينبغي أن يتصفح ذلك فيها، فإن وجد بها وإلا لا يجترئ على الإفتاء بها.
. أن تكون المسائل التي يأخذها موافقة للأصول المعتمدة.
. أنه لا يجوز الأخذ إلا من كان أهلاً لذلك .
. من كونه يتميز بسعة العلم ودقة النظر، وقوة الحفظ.
. أن يراجع المطولات من الشروح والحواشي وغيرها ؛ للاطلاع على ضوابط المسألة وتقييداتها. وتمامه في «المدخل ( ص ٢٤٣) ، و تذكرة الراشد» (ص ۹۸ - ۹۹»، و«المنهج الفقهي للإمام اللكنوي»(ص۱۷۱)، وغيرها.
(3) The guidelines and conditions for taking from non-reliable books are: 1. That what he takes does not contradict what is in the reliable books. Al-Lakhnawi said in al-Nafi' al-Kabir (p. 26): 'If a issue is found in a book for which there is no trace in the relied-upon books, one should inspect it there. If it is found there, otherwise he should not dare to give fatwa with it.' 2. That the issues he takes conform to the relied-upon principles. 3. That it is not permissible to take except from one who is qualified for that. 4. That he be distinguished by extensive knowledge, precise perception, and strong memory. 5. That he refer to the detailed commentaries, glosses, and others to learn the controls of the issue and its restrictions. And its completion is in al-Madkhal (p. 243), Tadhkirat al-Rashid (pp. 98-99), and al-Manhaj al-Fiqhi li'l-Imam al-Lakhnawi (p. 171), and others.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents five conditions for using non-reliable fiqh books (like the criticized Khulasat al-Kaydani). First, any ruling derived must not contradict established reliable books. Second, the rulings must agree with the basic principles (usul) of the madhhab. Third, only a qualified person (an expert in the madhhab) may extract rulings from such books. Fourth, the person must have wide knowledge, precise reasoning, and strong memory. Fifth, one must consult the longer commentaries and glosses to understand the parameters and restrictions of the issue. These conditions ensure that the weak material in such books is not taken at face value without verification.

Key Terms
الكتب المعتبرة (al-kutub al-muʿtabarah): The reliable, authoritative books of the Hanafi school that are the basis for fatwa.
الإفتاء (al-iftāʾ): Giving a legal ruling (fatwa), which requires knowledge and authority.
الكتب غير المعتبرة (al-kutub ghayr al-muʿtabarah): Books that are not part of the relied-upon corpus; they may contain weak or unverified rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the conditions listed, what should a person do if they find a ruling in a non-mu'tabar book that has no trace in the reliable books?
A) They may still give fatwa if they find it convincing.
B) They should inspect the reliable books for the ruling; if not found, they should not dare to give fatwa with it.
C) They should reject the non-mu'tabar book entirely and never use it.
D) They should assume the ruling is correct and issue fatwa.

Key Takeaway
Using non-mu'tabar books for fatwa is only permissible under strict conditions that ensure the ruling is verified and does not deviate from the established school.

Relying on Hadith from Books for Muftis
Explains when a mufti may rely on hadith from books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which a mufti may rely on a hadith from a book and explain the wisdom behind the division of scholarly labor.

Core Idea
A mufti may rely on a hadith if the book's author is a muhaddith or the hadith is traced to a reliable source with a trustworthy narrator.

This passage addresses a practical concern for muftis: How can they use hadith found in compiled books? The author clarifies that not all citations are equal. He sets out two scenarios where reliance is permissible and reminds us that hadith transmission and fiqh mastery are distinct disciplines. Understanding this ruling protects the integrity of both the hadith and the fiqh process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's scope
This ruling applies only to muftis when looking up hadith in books, not to laymen or direct transmission.
2
State the first condition
If the book's author is a muhaddith (hadith specialist), his mention of a hadith can be relied upon.
A muhaddith is someone specialized in hadith narration and criticism.
3
State the second condition
If the author attributes the hadith to a known hadith source and the author is trustworthy in transmission, the hadith can be accepted.
Attribution means citing the original hadith book (e.g., Sahih al-Bukhari).
4
Explain the rationale
Allah has given each discipline its experts. Muhaddithin focus on narration, fuqaha on fiqh. Each should be placed in their proper station.
The author emphasizes the importance of respecting scholarly hierarchies.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
A mufti finds a hadith in a book by a well-known muhaddith (e.g., Ibn Hajar). He may rely on it. If the hadith is cited with a chain from a reliable source like Sahih al-Bukhari, and the author is trustworthy, it is also acceptable.

الدراسة الرابعة: فوائد متفرقة للمفتي (1) صلى خلف عالم تقي فكأنّما صلّى خلفَ : ، وحديث : «علماء أمتي كأنبياء بني إسرائيل، إلى غير ذلك. نعم ؛ إذا كان مؤلّف ذلك الكتاب من المحدثين أمكن أن يعتمد على حديثه الذي ذكره فيه، وكذا إذا أسند المصنّف الحديث إلى كتاب من كتب الحديث، أمكن أن يؤخذ به إذا كان ثقة في نقله، والسر فيه : أنّ الله تعالى جعل لكل مقام مقالاً ، ولكـل فـن رجالا ، وخص كل طائفة من مخلوقاته بنوع فضيلة لا تجدها في غيرها. فمن المحدثين من ليس لهم حظ إلا رواية الأحاديث ونقلها من دون التفقه والوصول إلى سرها، ومن الفقهاء من ليس لهم حظ إلا ضبط المسائل الفقهية من دون المهارة في الروايات الحديثيّة، فالواجب أن ننزل كلاً منهم في منازلهم، ونقف عند مراتبهم، وقد أوضحت هذا البحث في رسالتي «الأجوبة الفاضلة الأسئلة عن الكاملة
The fourth study: Miscellaneous benefits for the mufti. (1) 'Praying behind a pious scholar is like praying behind...' and the hadith: 'The scholars of my community are like the prophets of the Children of Israel,' etc. Yes; if the author of that book is from the muhaddithin, it is possible to rely on his hadith which he mentioned in it. Similarly, if the author attributes the hadith to a book of hadith, it can be accepted if he is trustworthy in his transmission. The secret of this is that Allah Almighty has made for every position a statement, and for every art men, and has distinguished each group of His creations with a type of virtue that is not found in others. Among the muhaddithin are those who have no share except narrating hadith and transmitting them without understanding and reaching their secret, and among the jurists are those who have no share except mastering fiqh issues without skill in hadith narrations. So it is obligatory to place each of them in their stations and to stop at their ranks. And I have clarified this research in my treatise 'al-Ajwibah al-Fadilah al-As'ilah 'an al-Kamilah'.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling for muftis regarding the reliance on hadith found in books. The author first mentions two weak hadiths (commented in footnotes) to introduce the topic. The ruling is that a mufti may rely on a hadith if the author of the book is a specialist in hadith (muhaddith) or if the hadith is attributed to a reliable source and the transmitter is trustworthy. The author explains the wisdom: each discipline has its experts, and neither hadith nor fiqh scholars should overstep their bounds. Muftis should respect the hierarchy of knowledge and only use hadith from qualified sources.

Key Terms
محدثين (muhaddithīn): Scholars specializing in hadith narration and criticism
ثقة في نقله (thiqah fī naqlih): Trustworthy in transmission; a condition for accepting a hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a mufti rely on a hadith mentioned in a book?
A) If the hadith is famous among the people
B) If the book's author is a muhaddith or the hadith is cited from a reliable source with a trustworthy narrator
C) Only if the hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari
D) Never; muftis must only use their own direct transmission

Key Takeaway
A mufti may rely on a hadith from a book only if the author is a muhaddith or the hadith is traced to a reliable source through a trustworthy narrator.

Method of Learning

The Mufti's Duty When Hanafi Imams Differ
Rules for mufti's procedure in internal Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct procedure a Hanafi mufti must follow when Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ, and apply the hierarchy of sources to determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid mufti must follow the stronger evidence or majority of reliable later scholars, not his personal choice.

When the Hanafi school itself contains differing positions, a mufti cannot simply pick whichever opinion he prefers. This lesson explores the rules from classical Hanafi fatwa works that guide a mufti in navigating internal disagreement. You will learn how to prioritize evidence, when to follow the majority of later scholars, and when ijtihad becomes necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's capacity
Determine whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a muqallid. The rules differ: a mujtahid may weigh evidence independently; a muqallid must follow established positions.
The passage specifically addresses the non-mujtahid mufti.
2
Recognize the scenario of imam vs. Sahibayn
When Abu Hanifa is on one side and his two companions on the other, there is a reported view that the mufti may choose. However, the preferred view is that he must consider the strength of evidence.
This reflects the tension between following the school's founder versus the combined authority of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
3
Apply the hierarchy of sources
First, check for an explicit answer from the early imams. If none, see if the later scholars are unanimous. If unanimous, follow that. If they differ, follow the majority of reliable ones. If no textual answer exists, the mufti must exercise ijtihad.
The passage cites al-Hawi al-Qudsi for this hierarchy.
4
Understand the prohibition of arbitrary choice
A mufti who picks any opinion without weighing evidence is ignorant and violates consensus. He must consider changes in custom, people's conditions, what is convenient, prevalent practice, and strength of reasoning.
From the Fatawa of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
5
Conclude with the mufti's responsibility
The mufti must discharge his duty by either choosing the correct opinion himself (if qualified) or referring to someone more knowledgeable. He cannot act arbitrarily.
This protects the fatwa process from personal whims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل : إذا كان أبو حنيفة له في جانب وصاحباه في جانب فالمفتي بالخيار، والأول أصح إذا لم يكن المفتي مجتهداً). كذا في «الفتاوى السراجية)، واختار في «الحاوي القدسي » الاعتبار لقوة الدليل، وهذا فيمن له قدرة على الترجيح، فلا مخالفة بينه وبين كلام «السراجية»(4). (۳) وذكر في «الحاوي» أيضاً : «إذا لم يوجد في الحادثة عن واحد من أئمتنا جواب ظاهر، وتكلّم فيه المشايخ المتأخرون قولاً واحداً يؤخذ به، فإن اختلفوا يؤخذ بقول الأكثرين من اعتمد عليه كأبي حفص، وأبي جعفر، وأبي الليث، وغيرهم ممن يعتمد عليه، وإن لم يوجد منهم جواب البتة نصاً ، ينظرُ المفتي فيها نظر تأمل وتدبّر واجتهاد ؛ ليجد فيها ما يقرب إلى الخروج عن العهدة، ولا يتكلم فيها جزافاً». انتهى. . وفي فتاوی قاسم ابن قطلوبغا )) نقلاً . عن «الفتاوى الوَلْوَالجية»: «اعلم أنّ من يكتفي أن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاءَ من الأقوال أو الوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع». انتهى. وفي فتاواه» أيضاً في موضع آخر: «الناس بين مقلد محض، ومقلّد له الأهلية للنظر، فعلى الأوّل اتباع ما صححه المشايخ ، والثاني له الترجيح والتصحيح، وعليه العمل بما رجح عنده ، والإفتاء بما صححه المشايخ ؛ لأن السائل إنما يسأله عما هو المذهب عند أهله»). انتهى. . وفي «الدر المختار» أخذاً من «تصحيح القُدُوري» (٢) لقاسم بن قُطلُوبُغا (۳) : «إن قلت : قد يحكون أقوالاً بلا ترجيح، وقد يختلفون في الصحيح ، قلت : يعملُ بمثل ما عملوا به من اعتبار تغيّر العرف وأحوال الناس، وما هو الأرفق، وما ظهر عليه التعامل وما قوي وجهه ، ولا يخلو الوجودُ عمَّن يميّز هذا حقيقة لا ظناً، وعلى من لم يميّز أن يرجع لمن يميّز ؛ البراءة ذمّته» انتهى (1) (٤) المسألة
And it was said: If Abu Hanifa is on one side and his two companions are on the other, the mufti has a choice, and the first (view) is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid. Thus in 'al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya'. And he chose in 'al-Hawi al-Qudsi' consideration of the strength of evidence, and this applies to one who has the ability to weigh (opinions); thus there is no contradiction between it and the statement of 'al-Sirajiyya'. And it is mentioned in 'al-Hawi' also: 'If in an incident there is no apparent answer from any of our imams, and the later scholars have spoken with one opinion, it is taken. If they differ, the opinion of the majority of those who are relied upon, such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, and others who are relied upon, is taken. And if there is absolutely no textual answer from them, the mufti must ponder and exert his ijtihad in the matter to find what brings him closer to discharging his responsibility, and he should not speak in it aimlessly.' End quote. And in the Fatawa of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, quoting from 'al-Fatawa al-Walwalijiyya': 'Know that whoever is content that his fatwa or action conforms to a saying or a viewpoint in the issue, and acts according to whatever sayings or viewpoints he wishes without consideration of weighing (evidence), has shown ignorance and broken consensus.' End quote. And in his Fatawa also in another place: 'People are between a pure muqallid and a muqallid who has the capacity for independent reasoning. The first must follow what the scholars have considered correct. The second may weigh and correct, and he must act according to what he finds preponderant, and give fatwa according to what the scholars have considered correct, because the questioner only asks him about what is the madhhab among its people.' End quote. And in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar', taken from 'Tashih al-Quduri' by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: 'If you say: They sometimes narrate opinions without weighing, and they sometimes differ about what is correct; I say: He should act according to what they have acted upon, taking into account change in custom and the conditions of people, and what is most suitable, and what has become prevalent in practice, and what is stronger in its reasoning. And the (qualified) person who can truly distinguish this (not merely conjecturally) will not be absent from existence. And one who cannot distinguish must refer to one who can; thus his responsibility is discharged.' End quote.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on the methodology of ifta for a Hanafi mufti who is not a mujtahid. It begins with a scenario from al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya: when Imam Abu Hanifa holds one position and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the opposite, the mufti has a choice between the two views. However, the preferred view (al-asahh) is that he is not free to choose if he is not a mujtahid; rather, he must follow the stronger evidence. Al-Hawi al-Qudsi emphasizes that the mufti should give weight to the strength of the evidence, provided he has the ability to weigh. The passage then quotes al-Hawi: if no explicit answer is found from the early imams, the mufti follows the unanimous statement of the later scholars; if they differ, he follows the majority of trustworthy ones (e.g., Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth). If even the later scholars give no textual answer, the mufti must exert ijtihad to find a way to discharge his duty, but not speak arbitrarily. Next, from the Fatawa of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha quoting al-Fatawa al-Walwalijiyya: a mufti who simply follows any opinion without regard for evidence is ignorant and violates consensus. The same source distinguishes two categories: a pure muqallid must follow the correct opinions of the scholars; a muqallid with some capacity for reasoning may engage in tarjih and tashih, but his fatwa must still reflect the established correct view of the madhhab. Finally, al-Durr al-Mukhtar adds that the mufti should consider change in custom and people's conditions, convenience, prevalent practice, and strength of reasoning. If he cannot distinguish, he must refer to one who can. The overall ruling is that a non-mujtahid mufti is not free to pick any opinion; he must follow the strongest evidence or the majority of authoritative later scholars.

Key Terms
المفتي (al-mufti): In this passage, a mufti who is not a mujtahid, who must follow established positions of the madhhab and cannot arbitrarily choose opinions.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of weighing evidence to determine which opinion is stronger within the Hanafi school.
التصحيح (al-tashih): Determining which opinion is the correct (sahih) one within the madhhab, often done by later scholars based on evidence and practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if there is no explicit answer from the early imams and the later scholars differ, what should the mufti do?
A) Follow the opinion of Abu Hanifa only.
B) Follow the opinion of the majority of reliable later scholars.
C) Choose any opinion he likes.
D) Remain silent and give no fatwa.

Key Takeaway
A non-mujtahid Hanafi mufti must follow a prescribed hierarchy: weigh evidence, then follow unanimous or majority of reliable later scholars, and if still no answer, exert ijtihad with due consideration of context.

Who May Follow an Authentic Hadith Contrary to the Hanafi Madhhab
Critical refinement of a methodological principle with a concrete example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a Hanafi to follow an authentic hadith contrary to the madhhab and explain why a layperson cannot do so.

Core Idea
Only a mujtahid can follow an authentic hadith contrary to the madhhab; a layperson must remain a muqallid.

You have likely heard the famous principle: 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.' But does this mean any Hanafi can pick up a sahih hadith and change his practice? The great Hanafi scholars from Ibn Abidin to Ali al-Qari have clarified that this is only for those qualified to weigh evidence. This lesson unpacks the condition of ijtihad and shows why the layperson must stick to the madhhab—illustrated by a shocking example of a scholar who mistakenly declared the sunnah finger-pointing as haram.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Apparent Principle
Identify the saying 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' and its apparent meaning that any sahih hadith overrides the madhhab.
This is often misunderstood as a blanket permission.
2
Discover the Essential Qualification
Read Ibn Abidin's qualification: it is only for those with 'ahliyyat al-nazar'—the ability to analyze texts and distinguish abrogation, specification, etc.
Without this, religion becomes a plaything.
3
Apply to the Al-Kaydani Case
See how a scholar without proper ijtihad mistakenly declared the sunnah finger-pointing as haram. The passage shows the gravity of such error.
Ali al-Qari considered it close to disbelief.
4
Understand the Wisdom of the Restriction
Quotes from Nawawi and Muhammad 'Awwamah reinforce that claiming a hadith as the madhhab's position requires near-ijtihad or sound knowledge of the imam's methodology.
The madhhab is a coherent system, not a collection of isolated hadith.
5
Formulate the Operative Rule
State the mufta bihi: a lay muqallid must follow the madhhab; a mujtahid may follow the hadith if it meets the criteria, and his action does not remove him from the Hanafi fold.
This preserves both ijtihad and taqlid.

يعني كلام الشافعي له فيمن له رتبة الاجتهاد في المذهب. وشرطه أن يغلب على ظنه أن الشافعي له لم يقف على هذا الحديث، أو لم يعلم صحته ، وهذا إنَّما يكون بعد مطالعة كتب الشافعي له كلها، ونحوها من كتب الأصحاب الآخذين عنه ، وما أشبهها ، وهذا شرط صعب، قل من يتصف به ، وإِنَّما اشترطوا ما ذكرنا ؛ لأن الشافعي له ترك العمل بظاهر أحاديث كثيرة رآها ، ولكن قام الدليل عنده على طعن فيها، أو نسخها أو تخصيصها ، أو تأويلها، ونحو ذلك». وقال العلامة محمد عوامة في أثر الحديث الشريف» (ص ٦٩) : «وخلاصة هذا الجواب من كلام هؤلاء الأئمة : ابن عابدين، وابن الصلاح، وتلميذه أبي شامة، والنووي، ثم القرافي، والسبكي : أنه لا يصل إلى رتبة ادعاء نسبة حكم ما إلى مذهب الشافعي وغيره بناء على قوله المذكور إلا من وصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد أو قاربها. وبهذا يتبين : أنه لا يحق لأمثالنا أن يعمل بمجرد وقوفه على حديث ما - ولو صحيحاً - ويدعي أنه مذهب للشافعي أو غيره ، وأنه إذا عمل به فقد عمل بمذهب فقهي معتبر لإمام معتمد ...». وتمام تحقيق هذا البحث في كتابي المدخل إلى دراسة الفقه الإسلامي»(ص٢٠٧ - ٢١٤). (۱) هذه اللفظ لم يصح إلا عن الإمام الشافعي الله وهو بيان منه لأصول مذهبه في الاستنباط، وهو الحديث الصحيح وإن خالف عمل أهل المدينة أو عموم البلوى وغيرها من الشروط التي شرطها الحنفية والشافعية للعمل بالحديث، والذي ورد عن الإمام أبي حنيفة : «إذا صح الحديث فعلى الرأس والعين، وهذا تأكيد منه أنه يلتزم ويتحرى في استنباط الأحكام الفقهية سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا أن له قواعده وأصوله في قبول الحديث. ينظر : لميزان الکبری (۱) : ٦٦)، و(مقدمة معنى قول الإمام المطلبي» (ص ۸) عن مناقب الإمام أبي حنيفة» للموفق ۱ : ۷۷، و«المدخل (ص ۲۱۱ - ۲۱۲).
The main text of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah. And in 'Sharh al-Ashbah' by Biryazada, quoting from 'Sharh al-Hidayah' by Ibn al-Shihnah: 'If a hadith is authentic and it contradicts the madhhab, one acts upon the hadith, and that becomes his madhhab, and his follower does not cease to be Hanafi by acting upon it, for it has been authentically reported from him; i.e., from the Imam.' (Footnote: from al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah, and the complete phrase includes: 'like the issue of muzara'ah, even though the mashayikh stated that the fatwa is according to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view, because he is the founder of the madhhab and the prime Imam.') Then: 'The statement is not absolute; rather it is restricted to one who has reached the level of independent reasoning (ahl al-nazar). Otherwise, religion would be a plaything in the hands of every ignorant person. And here are some texts from major scholars of Islam clarifying this...' Then quotes from Ibn Abidin, Abu Zur'ah al-'Iraqi, Abu Shama, and others. Then: 'And in Tazyin al-'Ibarah li-Tahsin al-Isharah by Ali al-Qari: Al-Kaydani was grossly mistaken when he said that pointing the index finger (during tashahhud) is among the prohibited acts (al-'ashr min al-muharramat) like the ahl al-hadith do... This is a great error, and had it not been for good opinion and interpretation, it would have been clear disbelief...' Then quotes from Nawawi and Muhammad 'Awwamah. (Additional footnote): 'This expression is only authentically reported from Imam al-Shafi'i, and it is an exposition of the principles of his madhhab in derivation. What is reported from Imam Abu Hanifah is: 'If the hadith is authentic, then [it is] upon the head and the eye.' This confirms that he committed to and sought the Sunnah in juristic derivation, but he had his own rules and principles for accepting hadith.'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the well-known Hanafi maxim 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.' The author clarifies that this principle is not absolute but is restricted to those who possess the qualifications for independent legal reasoning (ijtihad). The discussion begins by quoting Biryazada from Ibn al-Shihnah's Sharh al-Hidayah, which states that one can act upon an authentic hadith contrary to the madhhab and still remain Hanafi. However, the author immediately qualifies this: it applies only to one who has reached the level of ahl al-nazar (capable of textual analysis). To illustrate this, he cites Ibn Abidin's warning that such a person must be able to distinguish between abrogating and abrogated texts. He then quotes Abu Zur'ah al-'Iraqi, who says it is impermissible for a layperson to leave a hadith for the opinion of his imam unless he has mastery of hadith criticism, usul al-fiqh, and Arabic. Abu Shama al-Maqdisi adds that only a scholar of known ijtihad can act on the saying of al-Shafi'i: 'When you find a hadith contrary to my view, take it and leave my view.' The passage then turns to a concrete example: al-Kaydani's claim that pointing the index finger during tashahhud is among the prohibited acts. Ali al-Qari sharply criticizes this, stating that such an act is established from the Prophet's practice and to declare it haram is a grave error, bordering on disbelief. Finally, the passage quotes Imam al-Nawawi and Muhammad 'Awwamah to emphasize that claiming a ruling for a madhhab based on a sahih hadith requires ijtihad or near-ijtihad. The closing footnote clarifies that the statement 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' is authentically reported only from al-Shafi'i, while Abu Hanifa said: 'If the hadith is authentic, then upon the head and the eye,' indicating his commitment to the Sunnah but with his own methodology for accepting hadith.

Key Terms
مقلد (muqallid): A layperson who follows a mujtahid without knowing the evidence.
أهلية النظر (ahliyyat al-nazar): The capacity for independent legal reasoning, specifically the ability to analyze primary texts and understand the methodology.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): The maximum effort in deriving legal rulings from the sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin as quoted in the passage, who is permitted to act upon an authentic hadith contrary to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Any layperson who encounters a sahih hadith
B) Only those who have reached the level of ijtihad (ahl al-nazar)
C) Only the founder of the madhhab, Imam Abu Hanifa
D) All Hanafi muqallids

Key Takeaway
The principle 'if the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' is not a blanket permission; it is restricted to those with ijtihad, and the lay muqallid must adhere to the madhhab.

The Authority of Mafhum in the Hanafi School
Explains the rule that mafhum is a proof in juristic narrations but not in divine texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the authority of mafhum in divine texts and in juristic narrations according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mafhum is a proof in the jurists' speech but not in the Quran and Sunnah.

In the Hanafi school, the concept of mafhum (implicit meaning) is treated differently depending on the source. While the Shafi'i school gives weight to mafhum in the primary texts of Shari'ah, the Hanafi school restricts its authority to the statements of the Hanafi jurists themselves. This critical distinction has important practical implications for how rulings are derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts
The passage discusses mafhum in two contexts: divine texts (nusus) and juristic narrations (riwaya). Identify these from the text.
Divine texts include Quran and Sunnah; juristic narrations refer to the statements of Hanafi scholars.
2
State the Hanafi rule for each context
From the passage, state whether mafhum is a proof in each context according to the apparent madhhab.
In divine texts: not a proof. In juristic narrations: a proof.
3
Note the contrary opinion of Imam Muhammad
The passage mentions that Imam Muhammad allowed mafhum as a proof in divine texts. Recognize that this is contrary to the apparent madhhab.
This shows intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the rationale
Al-Hamawi's hashia explains why mafhum is a proof in riwaya but not in nusus. Understand the reasoning: in juristic speech, the implicit meaning is intended; in divine texts, it is not.
The difference is based on the intent of the speaker.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a statement from a Hanafi jurist or a verse from the Quran, determine whether the mafhum can be used as evidence.
Practice solidifies the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة الدراسة الخامسة في فوائد نافعة لمن يطالع الكتب الفقهية وغيرها لأصحابنا الحنفية • قال في «كتاب القضاء» من «الأشباه » : «لا يجوز الاحتجاج بالمفهوم في كلام الناس في ظاهر المذهب كالأدلة ، وما ذكره محمد له في «السير الكبير» من جواز الاحتجاج به فهو خلاف ظاهر المذهب». كما في «الدعوى» من الظهيرية» ، وأما مفهوم الرواية فحجّة». كما في «غاية البيان» من «الحج» ». انتهى وفي «حواشيه» للحموي : «إنّما كان المفهوم حجّة عندنا في الرواية دون النصوص ؛ لأن المفهوم فيها ليس بمقصودِ بخلافِ كلام الأصحاب، فإنّه مقصود، فيكون حجّة فيها، وهذا هو الفرق بينهما ، وإنّه قد خفي على كثيرين، فاحفظه
Benefit: The Fifth Study on beneficial benefits for those who peruse the fiqh books and others by our Hanafi scholars. He said in the Book of Judgment from al-Ashbah: 'It is not permissible to use mafhum (implicit meaning) in the speech of people in the apparent madhhab as a proof, and what Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir about the permissibility of using it is contrary to the apparent madhhab.' As in al-Da'wa from al-Zahiriyya. 'And as for mafhum al-riwaya (implication of narrations), it is a proof.' As in Ghayat al-Bayan from Hajj. End. And in his Hashiya, al-Hamawi said: 'Mafhum is a proof with us in narrations (riwaya) but not in the texts (nusus), because mafhum in them is not intended, unlike the speech of the jurists, for it is intended, so it is a proof there. This is the difference between them, and it has been hidden from many, so memorize it.'
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on mafhum (implicit meaning). In the primary sources of the Shari'ah (like Quran and Sunnah), mafhum is not a valid proof. However, when it comes to the statements of the Hanafi jurists (their narrations or transmitted opinions), mafhum is indeed a proof. The text contrasts this with a view attributed to Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir, which allowed its use in divine texts, but that is contrary to the apparent madhhab. Al-Hamawi's note explains the rationale: in juristic statements, the meaning is intended and precise, so what is implied is also intended, while in divine texts, the explicit wording is the focus. Students should remember this important distinction.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhum): The implicit or understood meaning that is not explicitly stated but inferred from the wording
ظاهر المذهب (zahir al-madhhab): The apparent or well-known position of the Hanafi school
مفهوم الرواية (mafhum al-riwaya): The implicit meaning derived from the transmitted statements of the Hanafi jurists

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In the Quran and Sunnah
B) In the speech of people generally
C) In the narrations (riwaya) of the jurists
D) In the rulings of judges

Key Takeaway
Mafhum is a proof in Hanafi juristic narrations but not in the Quran and Sunnah.

The Evidentiary Value of Mafhūm in Hanafi Fiqh
Explaining when mafhūm is acceptable evidence in Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the contexts in which mafhūm (implied meaning) is accepted as evidence in the Hanafi school and state the rulings for each context.

Core Idea
Mafhūm is accepted only from narrations and scholars, not from Quran or Sunnah.

In Hanafi legal methodology, implied meanings (mafhūm) are not automatically treated as proof. This lesson unpacks the classical ruling from al-Ashbāh and other sources, clarifying when mafhūm may be cited and when it must be rejected. You will learn the critical distinction between scriptural texts, narrations, ordinary speech, and jurists' statements, and how the intention behind each affects evidentiary value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of speech
The passage mentions: 1) ordinary speech (kalām al-nās), 2) scriptural texts (nuṣūṣ), and 3) narrations (riwāyāt) and scholars' statements (kalām al-aṣḥāb). List these.
Note that 'ordinary speech' includes any non-technical human communication.
2
Determine the ruling for each category according to the apparent madhhab
From al-Ashbāh: mafhūm is not a proof in ordinary speech or scriptural texts. From Ghāyat al-Bayān: it is a proof in narrations. Al-Ḥamawī adds that it is also a proof in jurists' statements.
The apparent madhhab (zāhir al-madhhab) is the mainstream Hanafi position.
3
Note the intra-madhhab disagreement
Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabīr permitted using mafhūm in all cases, but this is deemed contrary to the apparent madhhab.
This is a minority opinion (nawādir).
4
Understand the rationale from al-Ḥamawī
Al-Ḥamawī explains: in scriptural texts, the implied meaning is not the intended purpose; in scholars' statements, it is intended. Therefore, mafhūm is a proof in the latter.
This subtle point is often overlooked, as the text warns.
5
Recognize the status of mafhūm al-mukhālafa in narrations
Jāmiʿ al-Rumūz states that mafhūm al-mukhālafa in narrations is considered without disagreement, citing Ṣadr al-Sharīʿa. However, a contrary view exists (Ījārat al-Zāhidī). The correct position is that it is considered but probabilistically (aktharī, not kullī).
Also, al-Kāfī states that takhṣīṣ (specific mention) in narrations negates what is not mentioned, supporting the use of mafhūm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة
قال في «كتاب القضاء» من «الأشباه » : «لا يجوز الاحتجاج بالمفهوم في كلام الناس (۱) في ظاهر المذهب كالأدلة (٢) ، وما ذكره محمد له في «السير الكبير» من جواز الاحتجاج به فهو خلاف ظاهر المذهب». كما في «الدعـــوى» مــن الظهيرية»(۳) ، وأما مفهوم الرواية فحجّة». كما في «غاية البيان»(4) من «الحج» ».
انتهى
وفي «حواشيه» للحموي : «إنّما كان المفهوم حجّة عندنا في الرواية دون النصوص ؛ لأن المفهوم فيها ليس بمقصودِ بخلافِ كلام الأصحاب، فإنّه مقصود، فيكون حجّة فيها، وهذا هو الفرق بينهما ، وإنّه قد خفي على كثيرين، فاحفظه واحتفظ به. كذا في «الزهر البادي على فصول العمادي(1) » معزياً إلى عبد الـبـر بـن الشحنة». انتهى
وفي «جامع الرموز» في «كتاب الطهارة» : «إنّ مفهوم المخالفة في الرواية كمفهوم الموافقة معتبر بلا خلاف كما ذكره المصنّف ؛ أي صدر الشريعة في «كتاب النكاح» ؛ أي من «شرح الوقاية » ) ، لكن في «إجارة الزاهدي: إنّه غير معتبر، والحق أنه معتبر، إلا أنه أكثري لا كلي. كما في «حدود» «النهاية» ». انتهى
وفي «الكافي) في «باب صفة الصلاة»: «التخصيص في الروايات يدلُّ على نفي ما عداه». انتهى.
وفي حواشي الأشباه» نقلا عن «أنفع الوسائل» (٦) : «مفهوم التصنيف حجة». | انتهى
A benefit. He said in the Book of Judgments from al-Ashbāh: 'It is not permissible to use implication (mafhūm) as evidence in people's speech (1) according to the apparent madhhab, like the textual proofs (2). What Muhammad mentioned for himself in al-Siyar al-Kabīr about the permissibility of using it as evidence is contrary to the apparent madhhab.' As in al-Da'wā from al-Zāhīriyya (3). 'And as for the implication of a narration, it is a proof.' As in Ghāyat al-Bayān (4) from the Book of Hajj. End. And in its glosses by al-Ḥamawī: 'Indeed, implication is a proof for us in narrations, not in scriptural texts; because the implication in them is not intended, unlike the speech of the scholars (al-aṣḥāb), for it is intended, so it is a proof therein. This is the difference between them, and it has been hidden from many, so preserve it and keep it.' Thus in al-Zahr al-Bādī ʿalā Fuṣūl al-ʿImādī (1) attributed to ʿAbd al-Barr ibn al-Shiḥna. End. And in Jāmiʿ al-Rumūz in the Book of Purification: 'Indeed, the implication of opposition (mafhūm al-mukhālafa) in narrations, like the implication of agreement (mafhūm al-muwāfaqa), is considered without disagreement, as the author mentioned – meaning Ṣadr al-Sharīʿa in the Book of Marriage, i.e., from Sharḥ al-Wiqāya – but in Ījārat al-Zāhidī: it is not considered. The truth is that it is considered, but it is probabilistic, not universal. As in Ḥudūd al-Nihāya.' End. And in al-Kāfī, in the Chapter on the Description of Prayer: 'Specific mention (takhṣīṣ) in narrations indicates the negation of what is other than it.' End. And in the glosses of al-Ashbāh, transmitted from Anfaʿ al-Wasā'il (6): 'The implication of classification (mafhūm al-taṣnīf) is a proof.' End.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a collection of benefits (fawā'id) concerning the legal value of implied meaning (mafhūm) in Hanafi jurisprudence. The first quote from al-Ashbāh states the rule: mafhūm in ordinary speech (kalām al-nās) is not a valid proof, in line with the apparent madhhab. This is analogous to how scriptural texts (adilla) are treated. However, Imam Muhammad's view in al-Siyar al-Kabīr allows using mafhūm, but this is deemed contrary to the mainstream position. The text then distinguishes between mafhūm in human speech and mafhūm in narrations (riwāyāt), the latter being a valid proof. Al-Ḥamawī explains the rationale: in scriptural texts (nuṣūṣ), the implied meaning is not the intended purpose, while in the statements of jurists (aṣḥāb) it is intended, hence it is a proof. This difference is crucial and often overlooked. Next, from Jāmiʿ al-Rumūz, we learn that mafhūm al-mukhālafa (opposite implication) in narrations is treated like mafhūm al-muwāfaqa (correlative implication) without disagreement, as affirmed by Ṣadr al-Sharīʿa. However, a contrary view exists in Ījārat al-Zāhidī, but the correct position is that it is considered, albeit on a probabilistic basis, not universal. Then, al-Kāfī adds that takhṣīṣ (specific mention) in narrations negates what is not mentioned. Finally, the glosses of al-Ashbāh report that mafhūm al-taṣnīf (implication of classification) is a proof. Throughout, the focus is on the technical application of mafhūm within Hanafi legal methodology.

Key Terms
المفهوم (al-mafhūm): Implied meaning; the understood but unstated significance of a statement that is used as legal evidence.
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhūm al-mukhālafa): The implication of opposition; deriving a ruling that the opposite of the mentioned case has a different ruling.
ظاهر المذهب (zāhir al-madhhab): The apparent or predominant position of the Hanafi school, as opposed to a minority view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rationale for why mafhūm is a proof in narrations but not in scriptural texts?
A) Narrations are easier to understand than scriptural texts.
B) The implied meaning is intended in scholars' statements but not in scriptural texts.
C) Scriptural texts are always clear, so mafhūm is unnecessary.
D) Narrations are less authoritative, so mafhūm is more readily accepted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mafhūm is a proof only in narrations and scholars' statements, not in scriptural texts, due to the difference in intended meaning.

The Technical Meaning of 'Qālū' in Hanafi Legal Texts
Definition of a technical term in Hanafi legal literature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the technical usage of the word 'qālū' in Hanafi fiqh works and explain its significance in indicating scholarly disagreement.

Core Idea
In Hanafi legal texts, 'qālū' signals disagreement among later scholars—not consensus or the preferred opinion.

When reading Hanafi fiqh books, you will often encounter the word 'qālū' (they said). At first glance, it might seem to convey a general opinion. However, this short benefit from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah reveals a crucial technical nuance: 'qālū' is deliberately used to flag that there is disagreement (ikhtilāf) among the later mashāyikh on that particular issue. Understanding this convention will prevent you from misinterpreting the strength or authority of the cited opinions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the term 'qālū' in a Hanafi fiqh passage
Identify the word 'qālū' in the text and note the immediate context—what ruling or issue is being discussed.
2
Recall the technical definition
Remember that 'qālū' indicates ikhtilāf (disagreement) among the later Hanafi scholars (mashāyikh). It does not express a consensus or the author's preferred view.
This is a conventional usage, not a universal rule; always verify with the broader context.
3
Determine the referent of 'qālū'
The term 'mashāyikh' refers to later Hanafi jurists, typically those after the early imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Identify which specific scholars or groups are implicated.
The exact identity of 'mashāyikh' can vary by text; consult the work's introduction or commentaries.
4
Evaluate the practical implication
Because 'qālū' signals disagreement, you cannot assume the stated opinion is the muftā bihī (relied-upon ruling). Further research is needed to determine which view is preferred.
Look for terms like 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' or 'huwa al-mukhtar' to find the authoritative position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة
لفظ : قالوا ؛ يستعمل فيما فيه اختلاف المشايخ. كذا في «النهاية» في «كتاب
A benefit. The word 'qālū' is used where there is disagreement among the mashāyikh. Thus in al-Nihāya in the Book of...
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This short benefit addresses the technical use of the word 'qālū' ('they said') in Hanafi fiqh literature. When authors use 'qālū', it signals that there is an ikhtilāf (disagreement) among the later scholars (mashāyikh) on the issue at hand. This is a convention for the attentive reader: the term 'qālū' does not indicate the majority view or a consensus, but rather the existence of divergent opinions among the senior jurists. The citation from al-Nihāya confirms this usage. Understanding this technical nuance prevents misinterpreting the weight of differing positions in later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
قالوا (qālū): A technical term used in Hanafi fiqh to indicate that there is disagreement (ikhtilāf) among the later scholars (mashāyikh) regarding a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the benefit (fā'idah) about the word 'qālū', what does its use indicate?
A) That there is a consensus among scholars.
B) That there is disagreement (ikhtilāf) among the mashāyikh.
C) That the ruling is the relied-upon (muftā bihī) position.
D) That the author is quoting a specific imam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh literature, 'qālū' is a technical term flagging disagreement among later scholars—do not mistake it for the authoritative ruling.

Pronoun Reference for 'Indahu' and 'Indahuma' in Hanafi Fiqh
Methodological note on pronoun usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the default imam referred to by 'indahu' and 'indahuma' in a Hanafi fiqh text and apply the exception when a third imam is previously mentioned.

Core Idea
Default: 'indahu' = Abu Hanifa; 'indahuma' = Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; exception after a third imam shifts the pair.

Hanafi fiqh works often use compact pronouns to attribute rulings without repeating names. 'Indahu' and 'indahuma' are key for knowing which imam's view is being cited. The default is fixed, but an exception arises when a third imam is mentioned earlier. Mastering this rule prevents misattribution and is essential for reading the primary sources correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pronouns
Note the words 'indahu' (عنده) or 'indahuma' (عندهما) in the text. If no prior imam is named, apply the default rule.
2
Apply the default for 'indahu'
If 'indahu' appears without a recent named imam, it refers to Imam Abu Hanifa. This is the standard assumption in Hanafi books.
Even if Abu Hanifa was not named earlier, the jurists consider him implied as the leading authority.
3
Apply the default for 'indahuma'
If 'indahuma' appears without a prior named imam, it refers to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani — the two main disciples (Sahibayn).
4
Check for a prior third imam
If before 'indahuma' the text mentions a third imam (like Muhammad or Abu Yusuf) in a different ruling, then the meaning of 'indahuma' shifts. For example, after 'ind Muhammad' (according to Muhammad), 'indahuma' means Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa.
The third imam is one of the two in the default, so the remaining two become the pair.
5
Verify with examples
Practice by reading actual sentences from Hanafi texts. Locate the pronouns and determine which imam(s) are meant using the rules above.
The passage gives two examples: after mentioning Muhammad, 'indahuma' = Abu Yusuf & Abu Hanifa; after mentioning Abu Yusuf, 'indahuma' = Abu Hanifa & Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة ضمير : عنده ؛ في قول الفقهاء هـذا الحكـم عـنده ، أو هذا مذهبه إذا لم يكن مرجعه مذكوراً سابقاً يرجع إلى الإمام أبي حنيفة، وإن لم يسبق له ذكر ؛ لكونه مذكوراً حكماً. وكذا ضمير: عندهما ؛ يرجع إلى أبي يوسف ومحمد ه إذا لم يسبق مرجعه، وقد يراد به أبو يوسف وأبو حنيفة ، أو محمد وأبو حنيفة له إذا سبق لثالثهما ذكر في مخالف ذلك الحكم، مثلاً : إذا قالوا : عند محمد له كذا، وعندهما كذا، يراد به أبو يوسف وأبو حنيفة : يعني الشيخين ، وإذا قالوا : عند أبي يوسف كذا، وعندهما كذا : يراد به أبو حنيفة ومحمد : يعني الطرفين
Benefit: The pronoun 'indahu' in the statement of the jurists 'this ruling according to him' or 'this is his madhhab' if its antecedent is not previously mentioned, refers to Imam Abu Hanifa, even if he has not been previously mentioned, because he is mentioned by way of ruling. Similarly, the pronoun 'indahuma' refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if its antecedent is not previously mentioned. And sometimes it may refer to Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa, or Muhammad and Abu Hanifa if a third party has been previously mentioned in opposition to that ruling. For example: if they say: 'According to Muhammad it is such, and according to them both (indahuma) it is such', it refers to Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa, meaning the two shaykhs. And if they say: 'According to Abu Yusuf it is such, and according to them both it is such', it refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, meaning the two parties.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage clarifies the standard usage of the pronouns 'indahu' and 'indahuma' in Hanafi fiqh texts. When a jurist says 'this ruling is such according to him (indahu)' without specifying who 'him' is, it always means Imam Abu Hanifa. Similarly, 'indahuma' (according to them both) means Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, there are exceptions: if a third imam (like Muhammad) has been previously mentioned, then 'indahuma' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage provides examples to illustrate this rule. This is crucial for correctly attributing rulings in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عنده (indahu): Pronominal phrase meaning 'according to him'; default referent is Imam Abu Hanifa unless a different imam is named immediately before.
عندهما (indahuma): Pronominal phrase meaning 'according to them both'; default referents are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Exception: when a third imam is mentioned before, it refers to the other two.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi fiqh book, if you see the phrase 'عندهما' without any prior mention of names, which imams does it refer to?
A) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
B) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
C) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
D) Muhammad and Zufar

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi texts, 'indahu' defaults to Abu Hanifa, and 'indahuma' defaults to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; when a third imam is mentioned first, 'indahuma' denotes the other two.

Distinguishing 'Indahu' and 'Anhu'
Distinguishes 'indahu' (madhhab) from 'anhu' (narration).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi technical terms 'indahu' and 'anhu' and state their significance for determining the authoritative madhhab position.

Core Idea
'Indahu' signals the madhhab; 'anhu' signals only a narration.

In Hanafi fiqh literature, precise terminology tells you the authority of a ruling. This lesson decodes two key phrases: 'indahu' (عنده) and 'anhu' (عنه). Mastering this distinction is your first step in reading Hanafi texts with scholarly accuracy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases
Locate 'indahu' and 'anhu' in a Hanafi text. They often appear after an imam's name, e.g., 'indahu' and 'anhu'.
Focus on the preposition: 'inda (at/according to) vs 'an (from).
2
Understand their meanings
'Indahu' means 'according to him' — his adopted madhhab. 'Anhu' means 'from him' — a narration that may not be his final view.
Think of 'indahu' as the official position, 'anhu' as a transmitted report.
3
Recognize the implications for authority
A ruling stated with 'indahu' is the mufta bihi (operative position) unless overridden. A ruling with 'anhu' may be weak or from a less authoritative narration.
In fatwa, 'indahu' is preferred over 'anhu'.
4
Apply to sample phrases
Take two statements: 'هذا عنده' and 'وعنه كذا'. Classify each and explain the difference in authority.
Practice with real examples from al-Hidayah or al-Quduri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة: الفرق بين : عنده وعنه ؛ أنّ الأوّل دال على المذهب، والثاني على الرواية، فإذا قالوا : هذا عند أبي حنيفة دلّ ذلك على أنه مذهبه ، وإذا قالوا: وعنه كذا، دلّ ذلك على أنه رواية عنه
Benefit: The difference between 'indahu' and 'anhu' is that the former indicates the madhhab (school position), and the latter indicates the riwayah (narration). So if they say: 'This according to Abu Hanifa (indahu)', that indicates that it is his madhhab. And if they say: 'And from him (anhu) such and such', that indicates that it is a narration from him.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This brief but important passage distinguishes two key terms in Hanafi juridical literature. 'Indahu' (عنده) means that the stated opinion is the established madhhab of the imam, i.e., the view he held and taught. 'Anhu' (عنه) means that the opinion is merely narrated from the imam, but it may not be his final or adopted position. This distinction is vital for determining the authoritative position (mufta bihi). A ruling narrated via 'anhu' may be less authoritative than one stated via 'indahu'.

Key Terms
عنه (anhu): A phrase indicating that a ruling is narrated from the imam, but not necessarily his final madhhab.
عنده (indahu): A phrase indicating the established madhhab position of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a text says 'وعن أبي حنيفة كذا' (And from Abu Hanifa such and such), what does this indicate about the ruling?
A) It is definitely his madhhab
B) It is a narration from him, not necessarily his adopted view
C) It is the fatwa position
D) It is rejected

Key Takeaway
Knowing whether a ruling is attributed with 'indahu' or 'anhu' is essential for correctly identifying the authoritative Hanafi position.

Zahir al-Riwayah: The Foundation of Hanafi Authority
Definition of Zahir al-Riwayah and its variations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Zahir al-Riwayah, list its component books, and identify the variations among Hanafi scholars regarding those books.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the authoritative core of Hanafi fiqh, comprising the six books of Imam Muhammad, with some dispute over the Siyar books.

The authority of a Hanafi ruling depends on its source. The most authoritative body of narrations is called Zahir al-Riwayah. Understanding which books constitute this category is essential for a mufti to prioritize rulings. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah defines Zahir al-Riwayah and presents the different lists given by later Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
The passage defines the technical term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and its equivalents. Recognize that it is a methodological clarification, not a ruling.
2
Extract the standard list of six books
The passage explicitly lists the six books of Imam Muhammad. Commit them to memory: Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Jami' al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Saghir, Al-Siyar al-Kabir, Al-Mabsut, Al-Ziyadat.
These six form the commonly accepted set.
3
Note the variations in the list
The passage reports that some later scholars exclude Al-Siyar al-Saghir, or both Siyar books, reducing the list to four or five books. Other sources restrict Zahir al-Riwayah to four books: Al-Jami'an, Al-Mabsut, Al-Ziyadat.
This variation affects which rulings are considered primary.
4
Understand the terminology overlap
The terms 'Zahir al-Riwayah', 'Zahir al-Madhhab', and 'Riwayah al-Usul' are used interchangeably. Recognize that any of these terms refers to this authoritative set.
In later texts, 'al-Usul' also refers to this corpus.
5
Apply the hierarchy for fatwa
Rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah are the primary basis for fatwa. Rulings from other books (Nawadir) are not relied upon unless supported. This passage lays the foundation for that hierarchy.
Remember: Muftas must prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة المراد بظاهر الرواية وظاهر المذهب وبالأصول في قولهم : هذا في ظاهر الرواية، وهو ظاهر المذهب، وهو موافق لرواية الأصول : هو الكتب الستة المشهورة للإمام محمد : «الجامع الصغير» و «الجامع الكبير» و«السير الصغير» و«السير الكبير» و«المبسوط» و«الزيادات». كذا في «كشف الظنون» و«رد المحتار». وذكر في تعاليق الأنوار على الدر المختار» : «إنّ بعضهم لم يعد «السير الصغير» ». وذكر الطَّحْطَاوي في «حواشيه»: «إنّ بعضهم لم يعد «السير» بقسميه منها». وقال في «نتائج الأفكار ) : «المراد بظاهر الرواية عند الفقهاء : رواية «الجامعين» و«المبسوط» و«الزيادات»، والمراد بغير ظاهر الرواية رواية غيرها». انتهى ومثله في «العناية»: إنّ المراد بالأصول «الجامعان» و«الزيادات» و«المبسوط»). وفي «مفتاح السعادة»: إنهم يعبّرون عن «المبسوط» و«الزيادات» و «الجامعين» برواية الأصول ، ومن «المبسوط» و «الجامع الصغير» و «السير الكبير» بظاهر الرواية ، و مشهور الرواية انتهى وقد مرّ بعض ما يتعلّق بهذا المقام في الدراسة الثالثة، وذكر هناك المراد برواية النوادر، ورواية غير الأصول، فتذكر.
Benefit: The intended meaning of 'Zahir al-Riwayah', 'Zahir al-Madhhab', and 'al-Usul' in their statement: 'This is in Zahir al-Riwayah', 'It is Zahir al-Madhhab', 'It agrees with Riwayah al-Usul' is: the six famous books of Imam Muhammad: Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Jami' al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Saghir, Al-Siyar al-Kabir, Al-Mabsut, and Al-Ziyadat. This is as in 'Kashf al-Zunun' and 'Radd al-Muhtar'. And it is mentioned in 'Ta'aliq al-Anwar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar' that some did not count Al-Siyar al-Saghir. And Al-Tahtawi mentioned in his 'Hawashi' that some did not count Al-Siyar with its two parts from them. And he said in 'Nata'ij al-Afkar': 'The intended meaning of Zahir al-Riwayah according to the jurists is the narration of Al-Jami'an, Al-Mabsut, and Al-Ziyadat, and the meaning of other than Zahir al-Riwayah is the narration of other than them.' End. And similar is in 'Al-Inayah': 'The intended meaning of al-Usul is Al-Jami'an, Al-Ziyadat, and Al-Mabsut.' And in 'Miftah al-Sa'adah': 'They express Al-Mabsut, Al-Ziyadat, and Al-Jami'an as Riwayah al-Usul, and [they express] Al-Mabsut, Al-Jami' al-Saghir, and Al-Siyar al-Kabir as Zahir al-Riwayah and Mashhur al-Riwayah.' End. And some related to this topic has already passed in the third study, and there the meaning of Riwayah al-Nawadir and Riwayah Ghayr al-Usul was mentioned, so remember.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage defines the technical term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (or 'Mashhur al-Riwayah'), which refers to the most authentic and relied-upon narrations within the Hanafi school. According to the generally accepted view, it consists of the six books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Jami' al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Saghir, Al-Siyar al-Kabir, Al-Mabsut, and Al-Ziyadat. However, there is some difference of opinion among later scholars: some exclude Al-Siyar al-Saghir or both Al-Siyars. A narrower definition found in some sources restricts Zahir al-Riwayah to four books: Al-Jami'an, Al-Mabsut, and Al-Ziyadat. The passage also equates 'Riwayah al-Usul' with this set. The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' carries the highest authority in the Hanafi school; rulings outside these books are considered 'Nawadir' (rare narrations) and are not relied upon for fatwa. Students are reminded that this topic was partially covered earlier.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authoritative body of narrations within the Hanafi school, consisting of the six (or four) books of Imam Muhammad.
رواية الأصول (Riwayah al-Usul): Synonymous with Zahir al-Riwayah, referring to the foundational narrations.
الكتب الستة (al-Kutub al-Sittah): The six famous books of Imam Muhammad that form the corpus of Zahir al-Riwayah.
السير (al-Siyar): The books on military expeditions and international relations authored by Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most common Hanafi definition cited in the passage, how many books constitute 'Zahir al-Riwayah'?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah consists of the six books of Imam Muhammad, forming the backbone of Hanafi fatwa, though some later scholars include only four.

Understanding 'Al-Asl' in Hanafi Legal Texts
Defines the technical term 'al-Asl' in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific book referred to as 'al-Asl' in Hanafi fiqh and explain why it is so named.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, 'al-Asl' is a proper noun for Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut, not a generic term.

When reading Hanafi fiqh works, you will often encounter the phrase 'ذكره في الأصل' (he mentioned it in al-Asl). This lesson clarifies that 'al-Asl' is not a generic reference to any source, but a specific title — the foundational work of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Knowing this helps you navigate the Hanafi textual tradition and understand the hierarchy of authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase
Locate the phrase 'ذكره في الأصل' (or similar) in a Hanafi text. This is the expression being defined in the passage.
The passage itself is a benefit (fa'ida) clarifying this phrase.
2
Note the author and book
Recognize that 'al-Asl' refers to al-Mabsut, a work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. He is a founding figure of the Hanafi school.
Imam Muhammad is the author of the six major books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the naming reason
It is called 'al-Asl' (the foundation) because Imam Muhammad composed it first, before his other major works: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
The order of composition establishes al-Mabsut as the primary source.
4
Cross-reference with other texts
When you see a citation to 'al-Asl' in later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Kanz), know they refer to al-Mabsut.
This is a convention; other schools may use 'asl' differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة. الأصل في قولهم : هذا الحكم ذكره في «الأصل» ونحوه: يراد به «المبسوط» تصنيف الإمام محمد، سمّي به ؛ لأنه صنفه أولاً، ثم «الجامع الصغير» ثم «الجامع الكبير»، ثم «الزيادات». كذا في «غاية البيان».
Benefit: The meaning of 'al-Asl' in their statement: 'This ruling he mentioned in al-Asl' and the like is: it refers to al-Mabsut, the work of Imam Muhammad. It was named thus because he composed it first, then Al-Jami' al-Saghir, then Al-Jami' al-Kabir, then Al-Ziyadat. This is as in 'Ghayat al-Bayan'.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage clarifies that when Hanafi jurists refer to 'al-Asl' (the foundation) in phrases like 'mentioned in al-Asl', they specifically mean Imam Muhammad's work al-Mabsut. The rationale is that al-Mabsut was the first major compilation by Imam Muhammad, serving as the foundation upon which his later works (al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat) were built. Thus, 'al-Asl' is a specific book title, not a generic term for any source.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-Asl): A specific book title referring to al-Mabsut by Imam Muhammad, not any generic 'source'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a Hanafi jurist says 'ذكره في الأصل' (mentioned it in al-Asl), which book is being referred to?
A) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
B) Al-Mabsut
C) Al-Ziyadat
D) Al-Siyar al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the term 'al-Asl' is a proper noun for Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut, the foundation of the school's transmitted rulings.

Defining Zahir al-Riwayah and Its Core Books
Quotes multiple authorities defining Zahir al-Riwayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Zahir al-Riwayah and identify which books are consistently included across different Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest authority in Hanafi fiqh, but its exact book list varies among scholars.

The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' appears frequently in Hanafi fiqh as the most authoritative layer of transmitted rulings. However, as this passage shows, authorities differ slightly on which books constitute this corpus. Understanding these variations is crucial for correctly prioritizing evidence in fatwa and study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
What exactly is Zahir al-Riwayah, and why does it matter? The passage seeks to define this technical term by citing multiple Hanafi authorities.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the foundation of the Hanafi school's transmitted knowledge.
2
List the different definitions from the authorities
Kashf al-Zunun and Radd al-Mukhtar mention al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. Ta'aliq al-Anwar notes some exclude al-Siyar al-Saghir. Nata'ij al-Afkar defines it as al-Jami'ayn, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. Miftah al-Sa'adah distinguishes between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah itself.
Note the overlap and discrepancies.
3
Compare which books are common and which are disputed
Al-Mabsut is mentioned in every definition. Al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Jami' al-Saghir are included by most, but al-Siyar al-Saghir is excluded by some. Al-Ziyadat appears in most lists.
Focus on the consistent core.
4
Understand the significance of Zahir al-Riwayah in the Hanafi school
Zahir al-Riwayah carries the highest authority; rulings from these books cannot be overridden by later fatwas unless based on stronger evidence. This classification is unique to the Hanafi school.
This explains why the exact list matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكبير» و«المبسوط» و«الزيادات». كذا في «كشف الظنون»(1) و«رد المحتار»(2). وذكر في تعاليق الأنوار على الدر المختار»(3): «إنّ بعضهم لم يعد «السير الصغير»». وذكر الطَّحْطَاوي في «حواشيه»: «إنّ بعضهم لم يعد «السير» بقسميه منها». وقال في «نتائج الأفكار»: «المراد بظاهر الرواية عند الفقهاء: رواية «الجامعين» و«المبسوط» و«الزيادات»، والمراد بغير ظاهر الرواية رواية غيرها». انتهى. ومثله في «العناية»: إنّ المراد بالأصول «الجامعان» و«الزيادات» و«المبسوط»). وفي «مفتاح السعادة»: إنهم يعبّرون عن «المبسوط» و«الزيادات» و«الجامعين» برواية الأصول، وعن «المبسوط» و«الجامع الصغير» و«السير الكبير» بظاهر الرواية، ومشهور الرواية. انتهى. وقد مرّ بعض ما يتعلّق بهذا المقام في الدراسة الثالثة، وذكر هناك المراد برواية النوادر، ورواية غير الأصول، فتذكر.

al-Kabir and al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat. So in Kashf al-Zunun and Radd al-Mukhtar. And it was mentioned in Ta'aliq al-Anwar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'Some did not count al-Siyar al-Saghir.' And al-Tahtawi mentioned in his Hawashi: 'Some did not count al-Siyar in its two parts from them.' And he said in Nata'ij al-Afkar: 'The meaning of Zahir al-Riwayah according to the jurists is the transmission of al-Jami'ayn, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat, and the meaning of non-Zahir al-Riwayah is other transmissions.' End. And similar in al-'Inayah: 'The meaning of al-Usul is al-Jami'an, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut.' And in Miftah al-Sa'adah: 'They refer to al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and al-Jami'ayn as Riwayat al-Usul, and to al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir as Zahir al-Riwayah, and Mashhur al-Riwayah.' End. And some related to this topic has passed in the third study, and there was mentioned the meaning of Riwayat al-Nawadir and non-Usul transmission, so remember.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage defines a technical term in Hanafi fiqh: Zahir al-Riwayah (the apparent transmission). The author collects definitions from multiple authoritative sources, showing slight variations in which books constitute this category. Kashf al-Zunun and Radd al-Mukhtar mention the books al-Kabir (meaning al-Jami' al-Kabir), al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. Ta'aliq al-Anwar notes that some exclude al-Siyar al-Saghir. Al-Tahtawi mentions that some exclude both parts of al-Siyar. Nata'ij al-Afkar defines Zahir al-Riwayah as the transmission of the two Jami's, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat, with non-Zahir being other transmissions. Al-'Inayah agrees, calling these al-Usul (the fundamentals). Miftah al-Sa'adah distinguishes between Riwayat al-Usul (the same books) and Zahir al-Riwayah (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir), adding Mashhur al-Riwayah (well-known transmission). The passage ends by reminding the reader of earlier discussion on Riwayat al-Nawadir.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The collection of six books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the authoritative transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school.
رواية الأصول (Riwayat al-Usul): Transmission of the fundamental books: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and the two Jami's.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Transmission of rare rulings not found in Zahir al-Riwayah, typically from other compilations of Imam Muhammad or his students.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following books is consistently included in Zahir al-Riwayah according to all authorities mentioned?
A) al-Siyar al-Saghir
B) al-Jami' al-Kabir
C) al-Kafi
D) al-Mabsut

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the authoritative transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school, comprising certain core books by Imam Muhammad, though authorities differ slightly on the exact list.

The Term 'al-Asl' in Hanafi Fiqh: A Proper Noun for al-Mabsut
Explains that 'al-Asl' is a proper noun for al-Mabsut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the technical term 'al-Asl' in a Hanafi text and state that it refers to Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut, distinguishing it from generic usage.

Core Idea
In Hanafi legal methodology, 'al-Asl' is a proper noun for Imam Muhammad's foundational work al-Mabsut.

When you encounter the phrase 'this ruling is mentioned in al-Asl' in classical Hanafi fiqh, it is easy to assume it means 'the original source' in a general sense. However, within the Hanafi school, 'al-Asl' has a very specific meaning: it is the title of a particular book authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson will clarify that technical usage and help you navigate the early Hanafi textual hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Phrase
Identify when a Hanafi text uses the term 'al-Asl' in a reference like 'ذكره في الأصل' or 'مذكور في الأصل'.
This phrase appears in many commentaries and fatwa collections.
2
Recall the Technical Meaning
Remember that in the Hanafi school, 'al-Asl' is a proper noun for the book al-Mabsut by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, his first major compilation.
Other schools use 'al-Asl' generically, but Hanafi usage is specific.
3
Understand the Chronology
Know the order of Imam Muhammad's works: al-Mabsut (first), then al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. Al-Mabsut is the 'original' foundation.
This sequence is mentioned in the source passage.
4
Distinguish from Later Commentaries
Later scholars wrote commentaries on al-Mabsut (e.g., by Khahar Zadah, al-Halwani) which are sometimes also called 'al-Mabsut' but are not the original. Understand that when a later author is cited, it may be his commentary, not the original.
The passage notes that these commentaries interweave the commentator's words with Muhammad's.
5
Apply in Reading
When reading a Hanafi text, if you see a reference to 'al-Asl', use this knowledge to locate the correct source. If you see a reference to a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir (e.g., by Qadi Khan), understand it means the commentary, not the matn.
This skill prevents confusion between original texts and their exegeses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة. الأصل في قولهم : هذا الحكم ذكره في «الأصل» ونحوه: يراد به «المبسوط» تصنيف الإمام محمد، سمّي به؛ لأنه صنفه أولاً، ثم «الجامع الصغير» ثم «الجامع الكبير»، ثم «الزيادات». كذا في «غاية البيان». وذكر بيري زاده في «شرح الأشباه» وغيرُه : «إنّ «المبسوط» شرحه جماعة من المتأخرين مثل : شيخ الإسلام المعروف بخواهَر زَادَه ، ويسمى «المبسوط الكبير»، وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وغيرهما ، ومبسوطاتهم شروح في الحقيقة، ذكروها مختلطة بكلام محمد كما فعل شراحُ «الجامع الصغير» مثل : فخـر الإسلام، وقاضي خان، فيقال : ذكره قاضي خان في الجامع الصغير» والمراد «شرحه»، وكذا في غيره». انتهى ملخصاً).
(1) ينظر: رد المحتار (1) : (75) ، وكشف الظنون» (2 : 1580).
Benefit. The origin of their saying: 'This ruling is mentioned in al-Asl' and the like means al-Mabsut, the work of Imam Muhammad, so named because he authored it first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. And Biri Zadah mentioned in Sharh al-Ashbah and others: 'Al-Mabsut was commented upon by a group of later scholars such as Shaykh al-Islam known as Khahar Zadah, and it is called al-Mabsut al-Kabir, and Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani and others. Their Mabsuts are in reality commentaries; they presented them mixed with Muhammad's words, as the commentators of al-Jami' al-Saghir did, such as Fakhr al-Islam and Qadi Khan. So it is said: Qadi Khan mentioned it in al-Jami' al-Saghir, meaning his commentary, and similarly for others.' End, summarized.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage clarifies a common reference in Hanafi fiqh: when a jurist says 'this ruling is mentioned in al-Asl', it refers to Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut, his first authored work. The author then notes that al-Mabsut received later commentaries, including one by Khahar Zadah called al-Mabsut al-Kabir, and by Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani. These later works are mixed with Imam Muhammad's original text, similar to commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam and Qadi Khan. Thus, when one says 'Qadi Khan mentioned it in al-Jami' al-Saghir', it actually means his commentary. The passage helps students avoid confusion between original texts and their commentaries.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-Asl): A technical term referring to Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut, the foundational book of the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) al-Mabsut
C) al-Ziyadat
D) al-Kafi

Key Takeaway
The term 'al-Asl' in classical Hanafi works is a proper noun for Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut, not a generic reference.

By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct referent of 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi' in Hanafi commentaries and state its relationship to al-Kafi.

Core Idea
Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is not an independent work but a commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid.

When reading Hanafi fiqh commentaries like al-Hidayah, you will encounter references to 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi'. This lesson clarifies that this refers to Imam al-Sarakhsi's commentary on al-Kafi, not a separate work. Knowing this ensures you correctly navigate the Hanafi textual tradition.

Guided Path
1

Understand the relationship

4
Contextualize the reference
Commentaries on al-Hidayah and others use 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi' to cite this work. Knowing this helps locate the original source.
5
Verify the source

This reinforces the reliability of the identification.

Default Meaning of 'Karahah' in Hanafi Texts
Establishing the default legal meaning of the term 'كراهة'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default meaning of 'كراهة' in Hanafi texts and identify when the meaning shifts to karahah tanzihiyah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi texts, 'كراهة' by default means makruh tahrimi, not makruh tanzihi.

When you encounter the word 'كراهة' (dislike) in a Hanafi fiqh work, what does it legally mean? The default is not a mild dislike but a prohibitive one—an act that is sinful and must be avoided. This lesson unpacks that rule and its exceptions, based on the authority of al-Nasafi and Ibn Nujaym.

Guided Path
1
Step 1: Recognize the term 'كراهة'
Identify the term in a Hanafi text. Note that it is often used without qualification (mutlaqan).
2
Step 2: Apply the default interpretation
Unless there is evidence to the contrary, interpret 'كراهة' as al-karahah al-tahrimeeyah (prohibitive dislike).
This is the rule given by al-Nasafi and Ibn Nujaym.
3
Step 3: Check for exceptions
Look for explicit mention of 'كراهة تنزيهية' or contextual evidence that would indicate a non-prohibitive meaning.
If such evidence exists, the default is overridden.
4
Step 4: Confirm the ruling
If no exception is found, the act is ruled makruh tahrimi—close to haram and sinful.
This has practical implications for fatwa and daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكراهة إذا أطلقت في كلامهم فالمراد الكراهة التحريمية؛ إلا أن ينص على كراهة التنزيه، أو يدل دليل على ذلك. كذا ذكره النَّسَفِيّ في «المصفى»، وابن نُجيم في «البحر الرائق» وغيرهما.
Karahah (dislike) when used absolutely in their speech, what is meant is karahah tahrimeeyah (prohibitive dislike); unless they specifically mention karahah tanzihiyah (non-prohibitive dislike) or there is evidence indicating that. This is what al-Nasafi mentioned in 'al-Mustafa' and Ibn Nujaym in 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' and others.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This is a terminological rule essential for reading Hanafi fiqh texts. The passage states that when the word 'كراهة' appears without any qualification, it should be understood as 'كراهة تحريمية' (makruh tahrimi), which is dislike that is close to prohibition and incurs sin if done. Only if the text explicitly mentions 'كراهة تنزيهية' (makruh tanzihi) or there is contextual evidence does it shift to the less severe category. This distinction is critical because makruh tahrimi has legal consequences similar to haram, whereas makruh tanzihi is merely discouraged. The author cites major Hanafi jurists al-Nasafi and Ibn Nujaym as his sources.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimeeyah): Prohibitive dislike; an act that is sinful to perform but not established by a definitive proof, thus standing below haram.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyah): Non-prohibitive dislike; an act that is better to avoid but is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Karahah tahrimeeyah
B) Karahah tanzihiyah
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
When 'كراهة' appears unqualified in Hanafi texts, it means prohibitive dislike (makruh tahrimi) unless an exception is indicated.
